Why the Prophet is Called Sayyid Before Mawla
Sanusi explains why the Prophet is called sayyid before mawla in the creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical and theological reason why the Prophet is described as 'sayyid' before 'mawlā' in the Islamic creed.

Core Idea
In times of need, refuge comes before help — so sayyid precedes mawlā.

In the traditional creedal formulations, the Prophet is given two titles: sayyid (master) and mawlā (protector). But they are not placed arbitrarily. Sanusi explains a deep reason grounded in human psychology and divine order: we first turn to him for refuge, then he helps. This short lesson unfolds that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice the key terms 'sayyid' and 'mawlā'.
2
Understand the two roles
Identify that sayyid is the one sought for refuge, mawlā is the helper. Note the logical order: seeking refuge precedes receiving help.
This distinction is central to the argument.
3
Apply to the Prophet's mission
See how the Prophet fulfills both roles: guiding in this world and interceding in the Hereafter.
The passage mentions his guidance and his praiseworthy station.
4
Reflect on the supplication
Conclude with the prayer asking for benefit from his station. This shows the practical aim of the creedal priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قدَّمنا في أصل العقيدة وصفه عليه الصلاة والسلام بالسيد على وصفه بالمولى ؛ لأنَّ السيّد هو الذي يُفزَعُ إليهِ في كلِّ مُهِمَّ والمولى هو الناصرُ ، ولا شكّ أنَّ الفزعَ في المُهِمَّ إلى السيّدِ يكونُ أوَّلاً ، ونصرتَهُ لِمَنْ فَزِعَ إليه في نيلِ مُهِمِّهِ تكون ثانياً بعد فزعِهِ إِليه ، ولا شكّ أنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ مَفزَعُ الخلائق ، وناصرهم في الدنيا؛ بَيَّنَ لهم مِنْ طريقِ النجاة ، وعلَّمَهُم مِنْ أنواع الهداياتِ ، حتى تركهم على المَحَجَّةِ البيضاء التي لا غبار عليها، ومَفزَعُهُم وناصرُهُم في الآخرة؛ إذ له المقام المحمود هناك، والشفاعة المتكثرة المشفّعة، والمقالة المسموعة، والسؤالُ المُعْطَى، والجاه الأعظم، والمنزلة العليا، نسأل الله تعالى أن يَهَب لنا نصيباً وافراً مِنَ النفع بسيادتِهِ وجاهه الأعظم دنيا وأخرى
And we only gave precedence in the original creed (Aṣl al-ʿAqīdah) to describing him, peace and blessings be upon him, as 'sayyid' (master) over describing him as 'mawlā' (protector/patron) because the sayyid is the one to whom one flees for refuge in every important matter, and the mawlā is the helper. There is no doubt that fleeing in an important matter to the sayyid occurs first, and his help to the one who flees to him in attaining his important matter occurs second after his fleeing to him. And there is no doubt that he, peace and blessings be upon him, is the refuge of all creatures and their helper in this world: he showed them the path of salvation and taught them the types of guidance until he left them on the clear path that has no dust upon it. And he is their refuge and helper in the Hereafter: for he has the Praiseworthy Station (al-Maqām al-Maḥmūd) there, the abundant accepted intercession, the listened-to speech, the given request, the greatest rank, and the high station. We ask Allah the Exalted to grant us an abundant portion of benefit through his masterhood and his greatest rank, in this world and the Hereafter.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage explains why in the creed the Prophet is described as 'sayyid' (master) before 'mawlā' (helper). The reason is lexical and logical: the sayyid is the one to whom one turns for refuge in difficulties, and the mawlā is the one who then provides help. Since turning for refuge comes first, the title sayyid is mentioned first. The Prophet is both the refuge and the helper in this world and the Hereafter. In this world, he guided people; in the Hereafter, he will intercede. The passage concludes with a supplication for benefit from his station.

Key Terms
سيد
مولى
فزع
نصر
مقام محمود
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'sayyid' and 'mawlā' are synonymous titles for the Prophet.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'sayyid' refers to the one sought for refuge, while 'mawlā' is the helper, and the order reflects the logical priority of seeking refuge before receiving help.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Prophet called 'sayyid' before 'mawlā'?
A) Because sayyid is a higher rank
B) Because seeking refuge with the sayyid comes first, then his help follows
C) Because mawlā only applies in the Hereafter
D) Because sayyid indicates his lineage

Key Takeaway
The order of the Prophet's titles in the creed reflects the logical sequence of seeking refuge first and receiving help second.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an important matter in your life, do you first flee to the Prophet as your sayyid, seeking his intercession and example—or do you rely on your own planning before turning to him? What practical step can you take this week to make him your first refuge?

The Prophet is your helper (mawlā) after you flee to him. Are you truly allowing him to help you by following the guidance he taught, or do you selectively obey only what is convenient? Which command of his are you neglecting that, if obeyed, would bring you the help you desperately need?

Honestly examine your heart: do you truly long for that benefit, or are you content with a distant admiration? What would change in your daily life if you genuinely expected to receive his help in every important matter?

The Meaning of 'Seal of the Prophets'
Sanusi defines the Seal of the Prophets and lists its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the title 'Seal of the Prophets' and its logical implications for the finality of prophethood and messengership, as well as the honors bestowed upon the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH).

Core Idea
The Seal of the Prophets closes prophethood and necessarily messengership, completing all excellences in one final law.

Sanusi opens a key doctrine: what does it mean that Muhammad (PBUH) is the 'Seal of the Prophets'? The phrase is more than a title; it establishes the finality of prophethood. From this, Sanusi draws a logical conclusion about messengers, and then highlights the unique honors given to the Prophet and his community.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the literal meaning of 'Seal of the Prophets': that he is the last of them, completing the number 124,000.
Notice the specific number mentioned.
2
Trace the logical implication
Identify why Sanusi concludes that no messenger can come after the Prophet. Focus on the relationship between 'prophet' (general) and 'messenger' (specific).
He uses the logical principle: negation of the general implies negation of the specific.
3
Explore the honors
List the four honors mentioned: completion of all previous excellences, eternal law with no abrogation, warning from past nations, and the community as witnesses.
These honors highlight the Prophet's unique rank and the status of his community.
4
Connect to Aqeedah
Reflect on why this belief is essential—it safeguards the finality of revelation and the completeness of Islam.
This is a core belief in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى ( خاتم النبيِّينَ ) : أَنَّهُ آخِرُهُم ، وبهِ كَمُلَ عددُهُمُ الذي هو مئة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً ، فلا نبي بعده ، ومِنْ لازمِهِ : أَنْ لا رسول بعدَهُ ؛ لأنَّ النبيَّ أعمُّ مِنَ الرسول على الصحيح ، ونفي الأعم يستلزم نفْيَ الأخص ؛ فكَمَّلَ سبحانَهُ لنبينا ومولانا محمد عليه الصلاةُ والسلام جميع المحاسن التي تَفَرَّقَتْ في الأنبياء والرسل قبلَهُ ، وشَرَّفَ شريعته السمحة ؛ بأن جعلَ أحكامها متصلة بالآخرة ، لا ناسخ لها ولا مُبدِّلَ لها ، وأطلعَ أُمَّتَهُ المشرّفة على مساوي الأممِ الذينَ خلوا وعلى العقوبات التي نزلَتْ بهِم ؛ ليعتبروا بذلك ويرتدعوا عن المعاصي ولا يغتروا بالمهلة ومتعة الدنيا كما اغتر بذلك الذينَ هلكوا قبلَهُم ، فجعلَهم مولانا بفضلِهِ معتبرين لا معتبراً بهم ، ومتَّعظينَ وشاهدين على غيرِهِم لا مشهوداً عليهم ، وأظهر سبحانه محاسنَهُم لِمَنْ مضى مِنَ الأمم وسترَ مَساوِيَهُم ، بل نَوَّهَ المولى [؟] لا مُتَعَظاً بهم
And the meaning of 'Seal of the Prophets' is that he is the last of them, and with him their number was completed, which is one hundred and twenty-four thousand. Thus there is no prophet after him, and from this it necessarily follows that there is no messenger after him, because the prophet is more general than the messenger according to the correct view, and the negation of the more general necessitates the negation of the more specific. So Allah, glorified be He, completed for our Prophet and Master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, all the excellences that were scattered among the prophets and messengers before him, and He honored his tolerant law by making its rulings continuous until the Hereafter, with no abrogating and no changing for it. And He informed his honored community about the faults of the nations that passed away and about the punishments that befell them, so that they might take heed thereby and desist from sins and not be deceived by the respite and enjoyment of the world as those who perished before them were deceived. So He made them, by His grace, admonishers, not being admonished, and witnesses against others, not being witnessed against. And He, glorified be He, displayed their excellences to the nations that passed and concealed their faults; rather, the Master praised [?] they are not admonished.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage defines the meaning of 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' (Seal of the Prophets). Sanusi begins by stating that it means he is the last of them, completing the number of prophets (124,000). Therefore no prophet comes after him, and necessarily no messenger either, because 'prophet' is more general than 'messenger' (every messenger is a prophet but not vice versa), and negating the general negates the specific. Then Sanusi enumerates the honors bestowed on the Prophet: all excellences of previous prophets were combined in him; his law is eternal with no abrogation; his community is informed of past nations' faults to take warning; they are made witnesses over others, not against them; and Allah displays their virtues while hiding their faults, praising them.

Key Terms
خاتم النبيين
الرسول
النبي
الأعم والأخص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'Seal of the Prophets' only denies new prophets, but allows new messengers.
Correction: Sanusi shows that because 'prophet' is more general than 'messenger', negating prophets necessarily negates messengers, so no messenger can come after him.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi conclude that no messenger can come after the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH)?
A) Because the Quran explicitly states there is no messenger after him.
B) Because the number of messengers is also completed at 124,000.
C) Because 'prophet' is more general than 'messenger', and denying the general implies denying the specific.
D) Because the Prophet said he is the last of all messengers.

Key Takeaway
The Seal of the Prophets means Muhammad (PBUH) is the final prophet and messenger, completing all prophethood and bestowing unique honors upon him and his community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says Allah made this community admonishers, not being admonished. Are you living as an admonisher – actively learning from past nations' mistakes and warning others – or are you comfortable being admonished by the world's standards? What change do you need to make?
?
You have been given the complete and final law with no abrogation. Are you treating it as a living guide or as a historical artifact? What one ruling do you currently neglect that you will commit to implementing starting today?

Wisdom Behind the Death of the Prophet's Male Children
Sanusi explains the wisdom behind the early death of the Prophet's sons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the divine wisdom behind the early death of the Prophet's male sons and how it relates to his being the Seal of the Prophets.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sons died young to preserve their honor, not as a punishment.

This lesson explores a question that may arise: why did all of the Prophet Muhammad's male children die in infancy? Sanusi provides a theological explanation rooted in the Prophet's unique status as the final messenger. The passage you will read connects this historical fact to a verse from the Qur'an, showing that it was a mercy and a protection of their rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Let the author's own logic come through before you interpret.
Notice the conditional reasoning: 'if they had lived... then...'
2
Identify the key terms
Find the three key terms: حطيطة (lowliness), سن النبوءة (age of prophethood), and شبه العلة (quasi-cause). Understand their roles in the argument.
These terms are central to the argument.
3
Trace the argument structure
The passage has a conditional argument: if the sons had lived, they would be lower than other prophets' children; therefore they died. Then it cites the Quranic verse as evidence.
This is a rational justification based on divine wisdom.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Many think the deaths were a punishment. The passage corrects this: it was a mercy to avoid a greater loss of rank.
This ties back to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأجل أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام خاتم النبيين: مات أولاده الذكور كلهم صغارا، قبل أن يكونوا رجالا؛ لأنهم لو عاشوا حتى يبلغوا سن النبوءة ثم لم ينبؤوا كانوا في ذلك أحط رتبة من أولاد كثير من الرسل الذين خلوا؛ كإبراهيم ويعقوب وداود عليهم الصلاة والسلام، فلما ماتوا صغارا انتفت هذه الحطيطة، وإلى هذا أشار القرآن في قوله تعالى: {مَا كَانَ مُحَمَّدٌ أَبَا أَحَدٍ مِنْ رِجَالِكُمْ وَلَكِنْ رَسُولَ اللهِ وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّينَ} [الأحزاب: ٤٠]، فجعل سبحانه كونه عليه الصلاة والسلام خاتم النبيين شبه العلة لما نفاه من أبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام.
And because he, peace and blessing be upon him, is the Seal of the Prophets: all his male children died young, before they became men; because if they had lived until they reached the age of prophethood and then were not made prophets, they would have been in that case lower in rank than the children of many of the messengers who passed—like Abraham, Jacob, and David, peace be upon them. So when they died young, this lowliness was removed. And to this the Qur'an alludes in His saying, exalted: 'Muhammad is not the father of any of your men, but he is the Messenger of God and the Seal of the Prophets' (Q. 33:40). Thus He, glorified, made his being, peace and blessing be upon him, the Seal of the Prophets as if the cause for what He negated of his paternity, peace and blessing be upon him.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage gives a rational explanation for a particular historical fact: none of the Prophet Muhammad's male children survived to adulthood. The author presents this as a consequence of his being the Seal of the Prophets. The argument is: if any of the Prophet's sons had lived to adulthood, they would have reached the age at which prophethood is normally bestowed (around forty). But since no prophet comes after Muhammad, they could not become prophets. This would place them in a lower rank than the children of previous prophets who did become prophets (e.g., Isaac, Jacob, Solomon). To avoid this apparent inferiority, God decreed that all his sons die in infancy. Thus, the verse 'Muhammad is not the father of any of your men' is interpreted as implying that no son of his reached adulthood to be counted among men, and this is linked to his being the Seal. The author calls this a 'shibh al-illa' (quasi-cause) for the negation of paternity of adult men.

Key Terms
حطيطة
سن النبوءة
شبه العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The death of the Prophet's sons was a punishment or a sign of Allah's displeasure.
Correction: The passage explains it was a mercy to preserve their rank, not a punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did all of the Prophet's male children die young?
A) To punish the Prophet
B) To prevent them from becoming prophets
C) To avoid them being lower in rank than other prophets' children
D) To fulfill a prophecy

Key Takeaway
The early death of the Prophet's sons was an act of divine mercy to protect their rank, confirming his status as the Seal of the Prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a loss that seems painful or inexplicable, do you instinctively question Allah's wisdom or mercy? How does knowing that the Prophet's own sons died young — not as punishment but to preserve their honor — challenge your reaction to your own trials? Will you commit to pausing before complaining and instead seeking the hidden mercy?
?
You claim to believe in the Seal of the Prophets, but do you truly live as if no new revelation or way of life can surpass Islam? Or do you secretly admire and adopt values from other worldviews as if they could offer something better? This lesson shows that even the Prophet's sons could not have a higher rank than Islam's finality. Does your heart accept this with contentment, or is there a residue of doubt?
?
If you were in the Prophet's place, would you have been able to trust Allah's wisdom in losing your children? The Prophet endured this with patience and submission. Are you willing to surrender your most cherished plans and attachments to Allah, trusting that He is protecting you from a greater lowliness? Name one attachment you need to release today.

Wisdom in the Early Death of the Prophet's Sons
Sanusi explains the wisdom behind the early death of the Prophet's male sons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the divine wisdom behind the early death of the Prophet Muhammad's male children and how it preserves his unique rank as the Seal of the Prophets.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sons died young to protect them from being lower in rank than the sons of earlier prophets.

The early death of the Prophet's male children is often a source of confusion. In this passage, Sanusi clarifies that this was not a punishment but a profound mercy. By understanding the logic of prophethood and finality, we see how Allah preserved the Prophet's honor and the honor of his children. Let's explore this teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the logical flow and the key terms.
Pay attention to the Quranic citation.
2
Identify key terms and argument
Identify the key terms: خاتم النبيين (Seal of the Prophets), حطيطة (diminishment), شبه العلة (like a cause). Follow the argument: because Muhammad is the final prophet, if his sons lived to adulthood they would not be prophets, making them lower in rank than the sons of earlier prophets who became prophets.
The argument relies on the principle of finality of prophethood.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Examine how Sanusi uses Quran 33:40 to support his point. The verse negates the Prophet being the father of any 'men', linking it to his being the Seal of the Prophets.
This is an example of tafsir (Quranic interpretation) within kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأجلِ أنَّهُ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام خاتم النبيِّينَ : مات أولاده الذكورُ كلُّهم صغاراً ، قبل أن يكونوا رجالاً ؛ لأنَّهُم لو عاشوا حتى يبلغوا سِنَّ النبوءة ثمَّ لم يُنبَّؤُوا .. كانوا في ذلكَ أحطّ رتبةٌ مِنْ أولادِ كثيرٍ مِنَ الرسل الذين خلوا ؛ كإبراهيم ويعقوب وداود عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، فلما ماتوا صغاراً انتفَتْ هذهِ الحَطِيطة ، وإلى هذا أشار القرآنُ في قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ مَا كَانَ مُحَمَّدٌ أَبا أَحَدٍ مِّن رِّجَالِكُمْ وَلَكِن رَّسُولَ اللهِ وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠] ، فجعل سبحانَهُ كونه عليه الصلاة والسلام خاتم النبيِّينَ شِبْهَ العِلَّةِ لِمَا نفاهُ مِنْ أُبوّتِهِ عليه الصلاة والسلام للكبارِ الذينَ يُطلَقُ عليهِمُ اسم الرجال ، والنكته فيه ما سبق تقريره ، والله تعالى أعلم .
And because he, peace and blessings be upon him, is the Seal of the Prophets: all his male children died young, before they became men; because if they had lived until they reached the age of prophethood and then were not made prophets, they would be lower in rank than the children of many of the messengers who passed before, like Abraham, Jacob, and David, peace be upon them. So when they died young, this diminishment was removed. And to this the Quran pointed in His statement, Exalted is He: 'Muhammad is not the father of any of your men, but he is the Messenger of Allah and the Seal of the Prophets' [Al-Ahzab: 40]. So He, Glorified, made his being, peace and blessings be upon him, the Seal of the Prophets like a cause for what He negated of his fatherhood, peace and blessings be upon him, of grown men who are called men. And the subtlety in it is what was previously established. And Allah, Exalted and Glorified, knows best.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage explains the divine wisdom behind the early death of the Prophet Muhammad's male children. The author argues that since the Prophet is the Seal of the Prophets (خاتم النبيين), i.e., the last and final prophet, if his sons had lived to adulthood, they would not become prophets (as prophethood ended with him). They would then be of a lower rank than the sons of earlier prophets (like Abraham, Jacob, and David) who did become prophets. To avoid this diminishment (حطيطة) in comparison, Allah caused them to die young. The author cites Quran 33:40, which negates the Prophet being the father of any 'men' (i.e., adult males) and instead emphasizes his role as the Seal of the Prophets. This verse is presented as evidence that the Prophet's fatherhood of adult men is incompatible with his being the final prophet. The 'subtlety' (النكته) refers to this wise arrangement already discussed. The passage concludes with 'والله تعالى أعلم' (Allah knows best), a common expression of humility and acknowledgment that deeper wisdom may be beyond human grasp.

خاتم النبيين
حطيطة
شبه العلة
النكته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the early death of the Prophet's sons was a punishment or a flaw in his prophethood.
Correction: The passage shows it was a mercy to preserve their honor and protect them from rank diminishment, affirming the Prophet's unique status.

Checkpoint

A) Because the Prophet was sinful and his offspring were cursed.
B) To prevent them from being lower in rank than the children of earlier prophets who became prophets.
C) Because they were sickly and the Prophet prayed for their death.
D) To fulfill a prophecy about the end of the world.

Key Takeaway
The early death of the Prophet's male children was a divine mercy to protect them from rank diminishment, affirming his unique status as the Seal of the Prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Muhammad: Leader of the Prophets and Best of Creation
Sanusi argues that Muhammad is the leader of all prophets and the best of creation using two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence Sanusi provides for Prophet Muhammad's supreme rank among all prophets and creation, and the humility of other prophets in recognizing his station.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the foremost prophet, and all prophets will be under his banner.

This lesson examines Sanusi's argument for the unparalleled status of Prophet Muhammad. Drawing on a key hadith and the event of the Night Journey, Sanusi establishes that Muhammad is the leader of all prophets and the best of all creation. At the same time, he highlights the profound humility of the other prophets who honor this rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow: from the claim of Muhammad's pride to the two proofs, then the conclusion and the reflection on humility.
The passage combines doctrinal proof with moral lesson.
2
Identify the two proofs
Find the two specific pieces of evidence Sanusi uses to prove Muhammad's leadership: the hadith about the banner and the event of the Night Journey. Write them down.
These are physical and eschatological proofs.
3
Understand the conclusion
After presenting the proofs, Sanusi states that Muhammad is the best of creation and most honorable to Allah. Reflect on why this conclusion follows from the proofs.
The conclusion is explicit: 'أفضل المخلوقات وأكرمها على الله'.
4
Examine the secondary lesson on humility
Notice how Sanusi uses this topic to highlight the humility of other prophets. Compare their attitude to that of the angels prostrating to Adam. What does this teach about perfect character?
This shows that recognizing superiority does not diminish others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سيدنا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام هو فخر الأنبياء والمرسلين. وقوله : ( وإمام المرسلينَ ) أي : مُقدَّمِهم في جميعِ الكمالاتِ ومتبوعهم ، يَتعلَّقونَ بهِ في شدائدِ الآخرة وأهوالها المعضلاتِ ، وقد قالَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : آدَمُ فَمَنْ دُونَهُ تَحْتَ لِوَائِي يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ. وقد ثبت أيضاً : أنَّهُ تَقَدَّمَهُم وأَمَّهُم حِسّاً في ليلة الإسراء ، وذلك كلُّه دليل واضح على أنَّ هذا السيّد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضل المخلوقاتِ ، وأكرمُها على الله تبارك وتعالى ، وفيه أيضاً دليل على كمال تواضعِ رُسُلِ اللهِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام للمولى تبارك وتعالى و امتلاء صدورِهِم بهيبته ومحبَّتِهِ ، والتعظيمِ لِمَا عظَمَهُ ، والتشريفِ لِمَا شرَّفَهُ ؛ إذ لم يجعلوا عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ ما حَصَّهُمُ اللهُ تعالى بِهِ مِنْ عظيم فضلِهِ مانعاً مِنَ التواضعِ لِمَنْ آثَرَهُ اللهُ تعالى بمزيَّةٍ وحَصَّهُ بفضْلٍ على جميع العوالم ، وأخلاقُهُمُ الكريمةُ في هذا نظيرُ أخلاقِ الملائكةِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ في تواضعِهِم وسجودِهِم لآدمَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ.
Our master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, is the pride of the prophets and messengers. And his statement: 'And the Imam of the messengers' i.e., their foremost in all perfections and the one followed, they cling to him in the severe difficulties and terrible terrors of the Hereafter. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Adam and those beneath him shall be under my banner on the Day of Resurrection.' And it is also established that he preceded them and led them physically in the Night of the Ascension. And all of that is clear evidence that this master, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is the best of creation and the most honorable to Allah, Blessed and Exalted. And in it also is evidence of the complete humility of the messengers of Allah, peace be upon them, to the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, and the filling of their hearts with His awe and love, and magnifying what He magnified, and honoring what He honored; for they, peace be upon them, did not make what Allah had granted them of His great favor an impediment to humility towards the one whom Allah favored with a distinction and singled out with a virtue over all the worlds. And their noble characters in this are similar to the characters of the angels, peace be upon them, in their humility and their prostration to Adam, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage establishes the supreme rank of Prophet Muhammad among all prophets and creation. The author begins by calling him 'the pride of the prophets and messengers' and explains the title 'Imam of the messengers' (إمام المرسلين) as meaning that he is foremost (مقدم) in all perfections (الكمالات) and the one followed (متبوع). On the Day of Judgment, all prophets will gather under his banner, as stated in the hadith: 'Adam and those beneath him shall be under my banner.' Additionally, during the Night Journey (الإسراء), he physically led the prophets in prayer, indicating his leadership. These two proofs (the banner and the leading in prayer) are presented as clear evidence that Muhammad is the best (أفضل) of all created beings and the most honorable (أكرم) to Allah. The passage then draws a secondary lesson: the humility of the other prophets. Despite their high rank, they did not consider their own excellence as a barrier to honoring the Prophet Muhammad. This character mirrors that of the angels, who prostrated to Adam despite their own lofty station. Thus, the passage simultaneously proves the Prophet's supreme status and praises the humility of the other prophets and angels.

Key Terms
إمام المرسلين
الكمالات
تحت لوائي
ليلة الإسراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The superiority of Prophet Muhammad diminishes the rank of other prophets.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that other prophets showed complete humility and recognition of his rank, mirroring the angels' prostration to Adam, which shows that honoring superiority does not diminish one's own dignity.

Checkpoint
What are the two pieces of evidence Sanusi gives for Prophet Muhammad being the leader of all prophets?
A) He was born without a father and performed the splitting of the moon.
B) He will have the banner of praise on Judgment Day and he led the prophets in prayer during the Night Journey.
C) He received the Quran and was the last prophet.
D) He had many wives and conquered Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The essential point is that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation, as proven by his role as leader of the prophets in both this life and the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly honor the Prophet as the best of creation, or have you allowed other loyalties—to yourself, your desires, or worldly figures—to compete with that? How can you realign your heart to give him the rank Allah has given him?
?
When someone else is honored above you, do you feel humility or resentment? This passage shows the prophets themselves humbled before Muhammad. Examine your own heart: is there envy when a brother or sister is praised? What action will you take today to cultivate genuine joy for others' excellence?
?
If on the Day of Judgment all prophets will cling to Muhammad, what about you? Are you building a connection with him now through following his Sunnah and loving him, or are you distant? What one change will you make this week to draw closer to him?

Prophethood
beginner

The Prophet as Imam of the Messengers
Sanusi defines 'Imam of the messengers' and provides proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the Prophet being the Imam of the messengers and the key evidence for his superiority over all creation.

Core Idea
The Prophet is the foremost of all prophets in every perfection.

Sanusi explains the phrase 'Imam of the messengers' as the one whom all other prophets follow, especially in the terrors of the Hereafter. He cites two key pieces of evidence: the Prophet's own hadith about Adam being under his banner and the historical event of him leading the prophets in prayer on the night of Isra. This passage establishes the Prophet's supreme rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on imamate
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the definition and evidence. Notice the concise language.
Pay attention to the phrase 'Imam of the messengers' and how it is unpacked.
2
Identify the two evidences
Find the two pieces of proof Sanusi offers: the hadith about the banner and the physical leading on the night of Isra. Understand how each supports the claim.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that the Prophet is the best of all creation. Ask yourself why this conclusion follows from the evidence.
This conclusion is a central tenet of Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للكبارِ الذينَ يُطلَقُ عليهِمُ اسم الرجال ، والنكته فيه ما سبق تقريره ، والله تعالى أعلم . سيدنا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام هو فخر الأنبياء والمرسلين الكمالاتِ وقوله : ( وإمام المرسلينَ ) أي : مُقدَّمِهم في جميعِ الكمالاتِ ومتبوعهم ، يَتعلَّقونَ بهِ في شدائدِ الآخرة وأهوالها المعضلاتِ ، وقد قالَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : آدَمُ فَمَنْ دُونَهُ تَحْتَ لِوَائِي يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ (١) وقد ثبت أيضاً : أنَّهُ تَقَدَّمَهُم وأَمَّهُم حِسّاً في ليلة الإسراء (٢) ، وذلك كلُّه دليل واضح على أنَّ هذا السيّد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضل المخلوقاتِ ، وأكرمُها على الله تبارك وتعالى ، وفيه أيضاً دليل على كمال تواضعِ رُسُلِ اللهِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام للمولى تبارك وتعالى و امتلاء صدورِهِم بهيبته ومحبَّتِهِ ، والتعظيمِ لِمَا عظَمَهُ ، والتشريفِ لِمَا شرَّفَهُ ؛ إذ لم يجعلوا عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ ما حَصَّهُمُ اللهُ تعالى بِهِ مِنْ عظيم فضلِهِ مانعاً مِنَ التواضعِ لِمَنْ آثَرَهُ اللهُ تعالى بمزيَّةٍ وحَصَّهُ بفضْلٍ على جميع العوالم ، وأخلاقُهُمُ الكريمةُ في هذا نظيرُ أخلاقِ الملائكةِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ في تواضعِهِم وسجودِهِم لآدمَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام (١) رواه الترمذي ( ٣٤٨ ، ٣٦١٥) من حديث سيدنا أبي سعيد الخدري رضي عنه (٢) رواه مسلم ( ١٧٢ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه الله والسلام امتثالاً لأمر مولانا جل وعلا، وتعظيماً لما عظم ، وتكريماً لِمَا كرَّمَ ، وحبّاً لِمَا أَحبَّ . وأين هذه الأخلاق الكريمة الزكيَّةُ مِنْ خُلُقٍ إبليس الأحمق المحروم ؛ حيث أمره المولى العظيم مع الملائكة الكرام بالسجود لآدم فاستكبر ، ورأى لنفسِهِ الدنيَّةِ شُفوفاً على مَنْ فَضَّلَهُ المولى تبارك وتعالى (١) ، وأدركَهُ الزَّهْوُ والإعجاب بما ليسَ لهُ ولا يستحقُهُ ؟! وإنَّما هو محض فضلِ مِنَ المولى الكريم تبارك وتعالى ، وأخذ بجهله وقلة عقله وعدم حيائِهِ وسابقِ شقائِهِ يعترِضُ على مَنْ لا شريكَ لهُ في مُلْكِهِ ولا في حُكْمِهِ ، يحكم بما يشاءُ ، ويَخُصُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ بما يشاءُ ، لا اعتراض عليه ، ولا سؤال لأحدٍ عليه ، وهو الحكيم المحمود على كلِّ حالٍ . ويجب على كلِّ مؤمن : أن يقتفي آثار الطاهرين المطهَّرينَ مِنْ كُلِّ حمق ودنس ؛ مِنْ رُسُلِ اللهِ تعالى وملائكتِهِ الكرام صلَّى الله وسلَّمَ على جميعهم ؛ فيتواضع الله تعالى ، ويُعلِّمَ كُلَّ مَنْ رأَى مِنَ المولى العظيمِ إيثاراً له وتفضيلاً بخاصَّةٍ ؛ مِنْ علم أو عبادة أو خُلُقٍ جميل ، ولا يجعل ما خَصَّهُ هو به مولانا جلَّ وعلا مِنْ فضل مانعاً مِنَ التواضع لذوي الفضل ، والتعظيم لجنابِهِمُ الرفيع عندَ اللهِ تعالى ، فيَهلِكَ ويُسلَبَ (١) في ( و ) : ( شرفاً ) بدل ( شفوفاً ) ، والشفوف : الزيادة والتقدم هنا ، يقال : شفَّ عليه ؛ إذا زاد
For the great ones who are given the name of men, and the subtle point in it is what was previously established, and Allah Almighty knows best. Our master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, is the pride of the prophets and messengers of perfections. And His saying: 'And the Imam of the messengers' means: their foremost in all perfections and the one they follow, they attach themselves to him in the severe matters of the Hereafter and its terrible hardships. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Adam and those below him are under my banner on the Day of Resurrection.' (1) And it has also been established that he preceded them and led them physically on the night of Isra' (2). All of that is clear evidence that this master, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is the best of creatures and the most honored of them before Allah, Blessed and Exalted. And in it also is evidence of the perfection of the humility of the messengers of Allah, peace and blessings be upon them, towards the Master, Blessed and Exalted, and the filling of their hearts with His awe and love, and veneration of what He magnified, and honoring of what He honored; for they, peace and blessings be upon them, did not make what Allah Almighty had bestowed upon them of His great bounty an obstacle to humility towards one whom Allah Almighty had favored with a distinction and singled out with a virtue over all worlds. And their noble character in this is similar to the character of the angels, peace and blessings be upon them, in their humility and prostration to Adam, peace and blessings be upon him. (1) Reported by al-Tirmidhi (348, 3615) from the hadith of our master Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him. (2) Reported by Muslim (172) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him. Allah and peace in obedience to the command of our Master, Glorious and High, and veneration of what He magnified, and honoring of what He honored, and love of what He loved. And where are these noble and pure characters from the character of Iblis, the foolish one, the deprived? When the Great Master commanded him along with the noble angels to prostrate to Adam, he was arrogant, and he saw for his lowly self superiority over the one whom the Master, Blessed and Exalted, had favored (1), and pride and self-admiration overtook him for what is not his and he does not deserve?! It is only pure favor from the Generous Master, Blessed and Exalted. And he, in his ignorance, lack of intellect, lack of modesty, and prior misery, began to object to Him who has no partner in His kingdom nor in His judgment; He judges as He wills, and distinguishes whomever He wills with whatever He wills; there is no objection against Him, nor does anyone ask Him; and He is the Wise, the Praised in every state. And it is incumbent upon every believer to follow the traces of the pure and purified ones from every foolishness and filth: from the messengers of Allah Almighty and His noble angels, may Allah bless and greet them all; so that he humbles himself to Allah Almighty, and teaches everyone whom he sees from the Great Master's favor and preference with a special distinction—whether of knowledge, worship, or beautiful character—and does not make what our Master, Glorious and High, has specifically given him of virtue an obstacle to humility towards the people of virtue, and veneration of their exalted station before Allah Almighty, lest he perishes and is stripped (of blessing). (1) In (w): 'sharafan' instead of 'shufufan', and al-shufuf means increase and precedence here; it is said: shaaf 'alayhi, meaning he increased.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a theological reflection on the Prophet Muhammad's status as the Imam of the messengers and a moral exhortation on humility. The author begins by explaining the phrase 'Imam of the messengers' as meaning the foremost and the one followed in all perfections, especially in the terrors of the Hereafter. Evidence is given from the Prophet's own hadith that Adam and those below him will be under his banner on Judgment Day, and from the fact that he physically led the prophets in prayer on the night of Isra. This proves his superiority as the best of creation and most honored before Allah. The passage then derives a lesson on humility: the prophets did not let their own great status prevent them from humbling themselves before Allah or before others whom Allah had favored (like Adam). Their humility mirrors that of the angels who prostrated to Adam. The author then contrasts this with Iblis, who was arrogant, saw himself as superior to Adam, and objected to Allah's command out of ignorance and pride. The passage emphasizes Allah's absolute sovereignty and wisdom, and that no objection can be raised against Him. Finally, the author exhorts every believer to follow the example of the prophets and angels, humbling themselves before Allah and respecting those whom Allah has favored with knowledge, worship, or good character, lest they lose their blessings like Iblis. The passage thus combines doctrinal proof of the Prophet's excellence with an ethical directive to cultivate humility.

Key Terms
إمام المرسلين
آدم
الآخرة
هيبة

A) The hadith about Adam under his banner and leading them physically on the night of Isra
B) The Quranic verse 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' and the Prophet's miracles
C) The consensus of the scholars and the testimony of the angels
D) His lineage and his character

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad is the imam of all messengers, as proven by his hadith about being the banner bearer and his physical leadership in prayer on the night of Isra.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet is the foremost in every perfection, which of his perfections are you most lacking in your own character, and what is one concrete step you will take this week to embody it?
?
On the Day of Judgment, all prophets will be under the Prophet's banner. Are you living today as if you truly believe that following his sunnah is the only path to safety? Where have you compromised or neglected his example?
?
The Prophet physically led the prophets in prayer, showing his leadership is real and immediate. In your daily salah, do you pray with the awareness that you are following his leadership in every bow and prostration? What would change if you truly felt his imamate in your prayer?

Humility: The Character of the Prophets and Angels
Sanusi contrasts the humility of prophets and angels with Iblis's arrogance and draws a moral exhortation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophets and angels exemplify humility before Allah, in contrast to Iblis's arrogance, and the duty of believers to follow their example.

Core Idea
True greatness lies in humility before Allah and honoring those He honors.

Having established the Prophet's supreme rank, Sanusi now derives a moral lesson: the prophets did not let their status prevent them from humbling themselves before Allah and before those whom Allah has favored, like Adam. Their humility mirrors that of the angels who prostrated to Adam. In stark contrast, Iblis was arrogant and refused to obey, leading to his downfall. This passage exhorts believers to cultivate humility and avoid the destructive pride of Iblis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on humility
Read the Arabic passage that discusses the humility of the prophets and angels, and the arrogance of Iblis. Note the contrast.
The passage uses the example of the angels prostrating to Adam as a model of humility.
2
Identify the contrast
The author contrasts the 'noble and pure characters' of the prophets and angels with the 'character of Iblis the foolish'. Identify the key difference: humility vs. arrogance.
3
Understand the believer's duty
The passage concludes with an obligation: every believer must follow the example of the prophets and angels, humbling themselves and honoring those honored by Allah.
This is a practical takeaway.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that receiving special favors from Allah is a reason to feel superior to others.
Correction: The passage shows that the prophets and angels, despite their high rank, remained humble and did not let their favors become an obstacle to humility. Arrogance like that of Iblis leads to destruction.

What does the author present as the key difference between the character of the prophets/angels and the character of Iblis?
A) The prophets had more knowledge than Iblis
B) The angels obeyed while Iblis disobeyed out of humility
C) The prophets and angels were humble, while Iblis was arrogant
D) Iblis was created from fire, while angels from light

Key Takeaway
True honor lies in humility before Allah and respecting those He honors; arrogance like Iblis's leads to loss.

?
Iblis was expelled for a single act of arrogance. Where in your life today might you be refusing to humble yourself before Allah's command, big or small? What is the cost of that pride?
?
The angels honored Adam out of obedience and love. Is there a person in your life whom Allah has blessed, yet you find it hard to respect? What would it take for you to venerate them as the angels did?

The Humility of Prophet Musa and His Rank
Author relates Musa's humility with Khidr and discusses his rank relative to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Prophet Musa's humility with Khidr demonstrates voluntary virtue and that his rank is second only to Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
True greatness is shown in voluntary humility.

This passage invites us to reflect on the character of Prophet Musa, the interlocutor of Allah. Despite his immense status, he humbled himself before al-Khidr to acquire knowledge. The author uses this story to illustrate that humility is a virtue of the great, and then explains Musa's lofty rank, second only to Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of Musa and Khidr
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the key phrases showing humility.
Pay attention to Musa's use of a question form and his promise of obedience.
2
Identify the lesson on humility
Notice that Musa used a question form and promised obedience, showing voluntary humility.
3
Understand Musa's rank
Learn about Musa's special sessions with Allah and the statement that his rank is second only to Muhammad.
Reflect on the hadith of Ibrahim's excuse in intercession.

أغلظَ لَهُ في القولِ ؛ إذ وصفه بعدم استطاعةِ الصبرِ معَهُ .. جاوبه هو عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ بتواضع ولين ، والتزمَ لهُ أنْ يطيعه في كل ما يأمرُهُ بهِ ، كما هو شأنُ العبدِ معَ سيْدِهِ ؛ فقال عليه الصلاة والرتبةُ الفائقة من اصطفاء مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ له على الناس برسالتِهِ ، ومناجاتِهِ لهُ بلا واسطةٍ بكلامِهِ القديم الذي لا مثل له ، وبالمعجزاتِ الباهرة ، والآياتِ العظيمة القاهرة، وقد ثبتَ أَنَّ لهُ معَ اللهِ تبارك وتعالى ألف مجلس في حد المناجاة ، وكلَّ مجلس يُمْنَحُ له فيهِ مِنَ العلومِ ما يَخْرُجُ عن الحصرِ ، وثبتَ أَنَّهُ عند المناجاة يرفعُهُ ويُقرِّبُهُ حتى يسمع صريف الأقلام يُكتبُ بها في اللوح المحفوظ ، وإلى هذا أشار القرآن في قولِهِ تعالى : وقربنه بحيا [مريم : ٥٢] • وقد نص بعضُ الأئمةِ : أَنَّ رتبتَهُ في الفضل تلي رتبة أشرف الخلقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى ؛ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وهذا هو الذي يدلُّ عليه حديث مسلم في الشفاعةِ في اعتذار إبراهيمَ عليه الصلاة والسلامُ عندما تُطلب منه الشفاعة في الآخرة لأهلِ الموقف بقولِهِ : « وَكُنْتُ خَلِيلاً مِنْ وَرَاءَ وَرَاءَ »، قيل : معناه : وكنتُ خليلاً مِنْ وراء موسى كليمِ اللهِ ، الذي هو وراء سيدنا ومولانا محمد حبيب الله فانظر يا أخي بعين الاعتبار إلى أخلاق هؤلاء الكرام ، وعظيم تواضعهم الله تعالى ، ومحاسنِ آدابِهِم مَعَ مَنْ لا يُضطَرُّونَ إِليهِ مِنْ
Humility towards one whom Allah has magnified. Let the intelligent person consider what the interlocutor of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) did with al-Khidr (peace be upon him): when he heard from the Great Lord, Blessed and Exalted, that He had distinguished him with knowledge from His own, he exerted his noble self by traveling to him until he met him, then he humbled himself to him in speech and asked him to teach him in the form of a question, not in the form of a command used in obligation and superiority. He (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Shall I follow you that you may teach me of what you have been taught righteousness?' (Al-Kahf 66). So he asked him in a manner of politeness in expression to be his follower learning from him. Then when al-Khidr (peace be upon him) met him by being harsh in speech, describing him as unable to be patient with him, he (peace and blessings be upon him) answered him with humility and gentleness, and committed to obey him in everything he commanded him, as is the condition of a servant with his master. He (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'You will find me, if Allah wills, patient, and I will not disobey you in any matter' (Al-Kahf 69). This humility occurred from this master in a matter he was not compelled to in its outward or inward, and he has great merit and lofty rank, from the selection of our Master, Majestic and Exalted, over people with His message, and His private conversation with him without intermediary with His eternal speech which has no likeness, and with the brilliant miracles and great overpowering signs. It has been established that he has with Allah, Blessed and Exalted, a thousand sessions in the level of private conversation, and in each session he is granted knowledge beyond enumeration, and it is established that during the private conversation He raises him and draws him near until he hears the screeching of the pens writing on the Preserved Tablet. To this the Qur'an refers in His saying: 'And We brought him near in communion' (Maryam 52). And some imams stated that his rank in merit comes after the rank of the most noble of creation and the most honored to Allah, our Master and Patron Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace). This is what the hadith of Muslim on intercession indicates in the excuse of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) when intercession is sought from him in the Hereafter for the people of the standing, in his saying: 'I was a friend from behind behind.' It is said: its meaning: I was a friend behind Musa, the interlocutor of Allah, who is behind our Master and Patron Muhammad, the beloved of Allah. So look, my brother, with the eye of consideration at the morals of these noble ones and their great humility towards Allah Almighty and the beauties of their etiquette with those they are not compelled to—
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is an exhortation on humility, using the example of Prophet Musa (Moses) with al-Khidr. The author begins by stating the theme: 'Humility towards one whom Allah has magnified.' Then he invites the reader to contemplate Musa's actions. Musa, despite his high rank as the interlocutor of Allah, traveled to meet al-Khidr, humbled himself in speech by asking to follow him in the form of a question rather than a command, and when al-Khidr spoke harshly, he responded with gentleness and promised obedience. The author emphasizes that this humility came from a great master in a matter he was not obligated to—highlighting voluntary humility. Then the author describes Musa's lofty rank: he was chosen for messages, spoke directly to Allah, witnessed miracles, and had a thousand sessions of private conversation where he heard the pens on the Preserved Tablet. Finally, the author cites an opinion that Musa's rank is second only to Muhammad, as indicated by a hadith where Ibrahim excuses himself from intercession saying he is 'behind' Musa, who is behind Muhammad. The passage concludes with a call to reflect on the humility and good manners of these great prophets, even with those they are not compelled to respect.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
Ibrahim declined intercession saying he was 'behind Musa who is behind Muhammad.' Do you truly see your own rank—and the ranks of the prophets—with such clarity that it reorients your humility towards others? Or do you secretly believe you are above learning from certain people?

Breaking the Circularity Objection in Proving Speech
Sanusi raises and answers an objection about circularity in using scriptural proof for divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi resolves the apparent circularity between scriptural proof and divine speech by distinguishing the nature of the miracle's indication.

Core Idea
The miracle indicates truthfulness, not identical to speech—no circularity.

This passage addresses a methodological objection: if we prove God's speech using scripture, but scripture's authority depends on miracles, and miracles depend on speech, aren't we going in circles? Sanusi clarifies the nature of the miracle's indication, showing the objection misunderstands the relationship.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the objector's claim that proving speech by scripture leads to circularity. Notice the chain of dependencies.
The objector assumes that miracle depends on speech in the same way speech depends on revelation.
2
Identify the dependence chain
Trace the objector's logic: scriptural proof depends on miracle, miracle depends on speech, so scriptural proof for speech is circular. Write down this chain.
This is a classic logical circle.
3
Grasp the key distinction about the miracle's indication
Sanusi answers that the miracle's indication is conventional (wadʿiyya) and only indicates the truthfulness of the prophet, not that God is the agent of the miracle directly. Understand how this breaks the circle.
The miracle is like a sign, not a direct speech act.
4
See how the circle is broken
Realize that the miracle does not depend on speech for its meaning; it depends on God's convention. The circle is not vicious because the miracle's indication is not identical to divine speech.
Thus, scripture can be used as proof without circularity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 ثبوت الكلام بدليل الشرع لا يلزم منه الدورُ ] فإن قلت : إثباتهم الكلامَ بالدليل الشرعيّ يلزم منه الدورُ ؛ لأنَّ الدليل الشرعيَّ موقوف على دلالةِ المعجزة ، وهي مُتوقفةٌ على الكلام ، بناءً على الصحيح مِنْ أنَّ دلالتها وضعية (۱) ؛ أي : تَتَنزَّلُ منزلة تصديقِ اللهِ تعالى لِمَنْ ظَهرَتْ على يَدِهِ بالقولِ فالجواب : أن تنزلَها منزلة التصديق بالقول إنَّما معناه : أنَّها تدلُّ على ما يدلُّ عليه القولُ مِنْ صدقِ الآتي بها ، لا أنَّ معناهُ : أَنَّ فاعلها الله
1 The affirmation of speech by scriptural proof does not entail circularity. If you say: Their affirmation of speech by scriptural proof entails circularity, because scriptural proof depends on the indication of the miracle, and it (the miracle) depends on speech, based on the correct position that its indication is conventional; i.e., it occupies the station of Allah's attestation by speech for the one on whose hand it appeared. The answer: That its occupying the station of attestation by speech only means that it indicates what speech indicates regarding the truthfulness of its performer, not that its meaning is that its agent is Allah.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector claims that using scriptural proof (Quran, sunna) to prove God's speech leads to circular reasoning because the validity of scripture itself depends on miracles authenticating prophethood, and miracles depend on speech (since a miracle is like God's verbal confirmation). The answer clarifies: a miracle's conventional indication (dalāla wadʿiyya) is not that God is literally speaking; rather, it indicates the same thing as speech—the truthfulness of the prophet. Thus, there is no true circularity because the miracle is not identical to divine speech in its function.

Key Terms
دور
دليل شرعي
معجزة
دلالة وضعية
صدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Proving God's speech from revelation is circular because revelation depends on miracles and miracles depend on speech.
Correction: The miracle's indication is not identical to speech; it only indicates the truthfulness of the prophet, so there is no circularity.

Checkpoint
How does Sanusi resolve the objection of circularity in using scripture to prove God's speech?
A) By denying that miracles depend on speech.
B) By stating that the miracle's indication is not the same as speech but only indicates truthfulness.
C) By saying that scripture itself is not proof.
D) By arguing that circularity is acceptable in theology.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi resolves the circularity objection by clarifying that the miracle's indication is not identical to speech but only indicates the prophet's truthfulness, thus breaking the dependence chain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you defend Islam to skeptics, do you rely on the miracle of the Quran as if it directly proves God's speech? How does this lesson require you to shift your argument, and does that shift make you more or less confident?
?
If the miracle only indicates the prophet's truthfulness, then your belief in the Quran as God's word ultimately rests on something beyond the miracle. What is that? Are you willing to follow that chain all the way, or do you stop at the miracle? Examine your heart: is your faith built on a secure foundation or a convenient assumption?

Prophethood

Prophet-Hood is Contingent, Not Obligatory or Impossible
Sanusi refutes Mu'tazila and Brahmins on prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sending prophets is rationally contingent (ja'iz) and not obligatory or impossible, and you will be able to refute the Mu'tazila and Brahmins' arguments.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a grace from God, not an obligation or impossibility.

Sanusi continues his discussion of contingent matters by addressing the sending of prophets. He affirms it is contingent, then refutes two opposing views: the Mu'tazila who say it is rationally obligatory, and the Brahmins who say it is impossible. This passage clarifies the Sunni position that prophethood is a gift from God, not a right or a logical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three positions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three distinct views: the Sunni position (contingent), the Mu'tazila position (obligatory), and the Brahmin position (impossible).
2
Examine the key claim: all benefits are by grace
Sanusi states that the benefits that come through prophets are purely by God's grace, and prophets have no effect. No one has a right to guidance or benefits from God.
This is the foundation for why sending prophets cannot be obligatory.
3
Analyze the Mu'tazila argument and its refutation
The Mu'tazila argued that God must send prophets because He must observe what is most beneficial (al-salah wa al-aslah). Sanusi dismisses this as corrupt, without elaborating further here.
The refutation relies on the earlier principle that God has no obligations from creation.
4
Analyze the Brahmin argument and its refutation
The Brahmins argued that sending prophets is impossible because reason alone can determine good and evil and arrive at God's rulings. Sanusi refutes by explaining that legal rulings depend on acts set by God as signs, which reason cannot know independently.
This highlights the limitation of reason in knowing divine commands.
5
Summarize the Sunni stance
Sending prophets is rationally possible (ja'iz) as a grace from God. It is neither obligatory (Mu'tazila error) nor impossible (Brahmin error). The benefits of prophethood are purely from God's favor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا مِنَ الجائزاتِ : بعث الله تعالى لرسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ لأنَّ ما قَدَّرَ اللهُ سبحانه وتعالى معهم مِنَ المصالح الدينية والدنيوية.. فبمحضِ فضلِهِ ، ولا أثر للرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام في شيء مِنْ تلك المصالح ، ولا حقَّ لأحدٍ على مولانا جل وعلا في هداية ولا في مصلحة دنيوية ولا أخروية . وأوجبَتِ المعتزلة عقلاً على الله تعالى بعثَ الرُّسُلِ ؛ على أصلهم الفاسد في وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح على الله تعالى ، ولا يخفى فساده . وأما البراهمةُ : فجعلوا بعثَ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام مستحيلاً ، ورأَوا أنَّ العقل يصلُ وحدَهُ بتحسينه وتقبيحه إلى أحكام الله تعالى ، ولا تخفى سخافة عقولهم في غايةٍ ؛ لِمَا عرفت أنَّ مرجع أحكام الله تعالى الشرعيةِ إلى نصب أفعال خلقها الله تعالى ، وجعلَها بمحض اختياره أماراتٍ على ما شاءَ مِنْ ثواب أو عقاب أو غيرهما ،
And similarly among contingent matters is God's sending of His messengers, peace be upon them, because what God appointed with them of religious and worldly benefits is purely by His grace, and the messengers have no effect in any of those benefits, and no one has a right over our Lord, Exalted and Majestic, concerning guidance or any worldly or otherworldly benefit. And the Mu'tazila made it rationally obligatory upon God to send messengers, according to their corrupt principle of the obligation of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial upon God, and its corruption is not hidden. As for the Brahmins, they considered the sending of messengers, peace be upon them, impossible, and they thought that reason alone, with its principles of good and evil, can arrive at God's rulings, and the stupidity of their minds is not hidden to the utmost; because you know that the source of God's legal rulings is to set up acts that God created, and He made them, by His pure choice, signs for what He wills of reward or punishment or other things.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage addresses the sending of prophets. Sanusi affirms it is a contingent matter (جائز), not obligatory. The benefits that come through prophets are purely by God's grace, and prophets themselves have no effect. No one has a right to guidance or benefits from God. Then he refutes two opposing views: the Mu'tazila argued that God must send prophets because He must observe the most beneficial (الصلاح والأصلح). Sanusi dismisses this as corrupt, referencing the earlier argument. The Brahmins (البراهمة) argued that sending prophets is impossible because reason alone can determine good and evil and arrive at God's rulings. Sanusi calls their view foolish, explaining that legal rulings depend on God setting up specific acts as signs for reward and punishment, which reason alone cannot determine.

Key Terms
بعث الرسل
جائز
فضل
المعتزلة
البراهمة
تحسين وتقبيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That reason alone can determine all religious rulings, making prophethood unnecessary or impossible.
Correction: Sanusi shows that legal rulings are based on acts God designates as signs, which reason cannot know; thus prophethood is needed as a grace.

Checkpoint

B) It is possible
C) It is impossible
D) It is uncertain

Key Takeaway
Sending prophets is a grace from God, not an obligation or something reason can deduce.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Sending Messengers is Permissible, Not Obligatory
Sanusi declares sending messengers not rationally obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sending messengers is a permissible act of God, not an obligation, and why any benefit from prophethood is purely by God's grace.

Core Idea
God is not obliged to send messengers; it is a gracious gift.

Sanusi begins by stating the correct Islamic position on prophethood: it is not a rational obligation upon God. He clarifies that any benefits from messengers are solely due to God’s grace, and no one has a right to demand guidance. This sets the foundation for refuting deviant views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words establish the point.
2
Identify the ruling
Notice that Sanusi first negates obligation (lā yajibu) and then affirms permissibility (min al-jā'izāt). This is the core teaching.
The term jā'iz is central.
3
Understand the reasoning
Recognize that benefits from messengers are by God's grace (bi-mahḍi faḍlihi), messengers have no causal effect, and no one has a right to guidance.
This protects divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجب على الله تعالى عقلاً بَعْثُ الرُّسُل لهدايةِ الخَلْقِ. وكذا مِنَ الجائزاتِ: بعث الله تعالى لرسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام؛ لأنَّ ما قَدَّرَ اللهُ سبحانه وتعالى معهم مِنَ المصالح الدينية والدنيوية.. فبمحضِ فضلِهِ، ولا أثر للرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام في شيء مِنْ تلك المصالح، ولا حقَّ لأحدٍ على مولانا جل وعلا في هداية ولا في مصلحة دنيوية ولا أخروية. وأوجَبَتِ المعتزلة عقلاً على الله تعالى بعثَ الرُّسُلِ؛ على أصلهم الفاسد في وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح على الله تعالى، ولا يخفى فساده. وأما البراهمةُ: فجعلوا بعثَ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام مستحيلاً، ورأَوا أنَّ العقل يصلُ وحدهُ بتحسينه وتقبيحه إلى أحكام الله تعالى، ولا تخفى سخافة عقولهم في غايةٍ؛ لِمَا عرفت أنَّ مرجع أحكام الله تعالى الشرعيةِ إلى نصب أفعال خلقها الله تعالى، وجعلَها بمحض اختياره أماراتٍ على ما شاءَ مِنْ ثواب أو عقاب أو غيرهما، ولا حسن في فعل ولا قبحَ يُوجِبُ له حكماً مِنَ الأحكام، ومَنْ عرف انفراده تعالى بإيجاد جميع الكائنات، ونفوذ إرادتِهِ فيها، مع التنزه عن الأغراض . . لا يخفى عليهِ فساد تلك المقالة الشنيعة، وبالله تعالى التوفيق. (۱) عُلَّقَ في (د): ( لأنَّ نفي السبب الذي هو الغرض . . ينفي المسبب الذي هو وجوب الصلاح والأصلح ).
It is not obligatory upon God, exalted, rationally, to send the messengers for the guidance of creation. And likewise among the permissible things: sending by God, exalted, of His messengers, peace and blessings upon them; because what God, glorified and exalted, has decreed with them of religious and worldly benefits is by the sheer grace of His favor, and the messengers, peace and blessings upon them, have no effect in any of those benefits, and there is no right for anyone against our Master, majestic and mighty, in guidance nor in any worldly or otherworldly benefit. The Mu'tazila made it obligatory upon God, exalted, rationally, to send the messengers, based on their corrupt principle of the obligation of observing the best and most beneficial (al-ṣalāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ) upon God, exalted, and its corruption is not hidden. As for the Brahmins, they made the sending of messengers, peace and blessings upon them, impossible, and they saw that the intellect by itself, with its self-approbation and disapprobation (taḥsīn and taqbīḥ), reaches the judgments of God, exalted, and the foolishness of their minds in extremity is not hidden; because you have known that the reference of the legal judgments of God, exalted, is to the establishing of actions that God, exalted, has created, and He made them by sheer choice signs for what He willed of reward or punishment or other than them. There is no beauty (ḥusn) in an act nor ugliness (qubḥ) that necessitates for it any judgment among judgments. And whoever knows His uniqueness, exalted, in bringing into existence all contingent beings, and the penetration of His will in them, along with being free from purposes (aġrāḍ) ... the corruption of that abhorrent statement will not be hidden from him. And with God, exalted, is success. (1) Annotated in (d): 'Because the negation of the cause, which is the purpose, negates the effect, which is the obligation of the best and most beneficial.'
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a combined doctrinal statement and refutation. First, the author declares that sending messengers is not rationally obligatory but permissible, because any benefit from them is by God's grace and the messengers have no causal effect; no one has a right to guidance. Then he refutes two opposing groups. The Mu'tazila wrongly made it obligatory based on their principle that God must do what is best (al-ṣalāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ). The Brahmins wrongly deemed it impossible, claiming reason alone suffices. The author counters that divine legal judgments are based on actions God creates and designates as signs, and there is no inherent good or evil in actions that necessitate a judgment. God is unique and free from purposes, so obligation is impossible. The footnote explains that denying purpose (gharaḍ) negates the premise of obligation.

Key Terms
جائز
واجب
عقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is rationally obligated to send messengers to guide humanity.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that sending messengers is a permissible act of God's grace, not an obligation.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, sending messengers is:
A) obligatory
B) permissible
C) impossible
D) recommended

Key Takeaway
God’s sending of messengers is a gracious act, not a duty imposed on Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God had never sent a messenger, what would your life be like right now? Knowing He was not obliged to guide you, how does this truth move you to gratitude? What will you do today to thank Him for His grace?
?
The messengers have no effect—all benefit is from God. Do you find yourself relying on any person, leader, or means as if they hold independent power? Where do you need to redirect your trust solely to Allah?
?
You have no right to any guidance or blessing from God—everything is pure grace. Has this caused you to feel entitlement instead of humility? Repent of any ingratitude and make a specific commitment to praise Allah for His unearned favors.

Refuting the Mu'tazila on Obligation of Prophethood
Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazila claim that sending messengers is obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila view on prophethood and why Sanusi deems it corrupt.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila wrongly made prophethood obligatory based on a flawed principle.

Sanusi now refutes the Mu'tazila, who claimed that God must send messengers because He must do what is best (al-ṣalāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ). Sanusi declares this principle fundamentally corrupt, setting the stage for the Ash'ari position of divine freedom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Note the concise condemnation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila principle
They base obligation on 'observing the best and most beneficial' (al-ṣalāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ). Recognize this as their core argument.
3
Recognize the refutation
Sanusi simply calls it corrupt (fāsid) without elaboration. Understand that in Ash'ari thought, God is not subject to external obligations.
The brevity implies the reader knows the standard refutation.

?

?

What does Sanusi's dismissal of the principle of al-ṣalāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ say about that assumption? How can you realign your heart to trust His wisdom without demanding explanation?
?
How does the truth that God is not subject to external obligations affect the way you pray or ask for things? Do you approach Him as someone who must answer you, or as the sovereign Lord who freely gives? What needs to change in your dua tonight?

Refuting the Brahmins’ Denial of Prophethood
Sanusi refutes the Brahmins who deny the possibility of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Brahmin denial of prophethood and Sanusi's refutation based on divine sovereignty.

Core Idea
The Brahmins rejected prophethood, claiming reason suffices; Sanusi affirms God's sole sovereignty.

Sanusi now tackles the Brahmins, who went to the opposite extreme by deeming prophecy impossible. They argued that reason alone can discern divine commands. Sanusi counters by highlighting that all legal judgments are based on God's creative will, not inherent good or evil, and that God is free from purposes. Anyone recognizing God's uniqueness will see the folly of the Brahmin view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the longer Arabic passage and translation. Notice the detailed argument.
2
Identify the Brahmin claim
They say prophecy is impossible (mustaḥīl) and reason suffices through taḥsīn and taqbīḥ.
3
Understand Sanusi's response
He argues that legal judgments are based on actions God creates as signs, not on inherent good or evil. There is no ḥusn or qubḥ that necessitates a ruling.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
God's uniqueness and freedom from purposes (aġrāḍ) negates any obligation, so the Brahmin view is absurd.
The footnote clarifies that denying purpose negates the premise of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Obligation of Truthfulness for Messengers
Defines truthfulness for messengers and its proof from miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why truthfulness is an obligatory attribute for messengers and how miracles serve as divine verification of their truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's stamp of approval on a messenger's truthfulness.

In this passage, Sanusi begins the discussion on prophethood by establishing a foundational attribute of messengers: truthfulness. He explains that everything a messenger reports must correspond to reality, and he provides the proof for this from the miracles God grants them. This lesson unpacks that proof and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on truthfulness
Read the first part of the passage up to the divine statement. Notice the concise definition of truthfulness.
The Arabic uses 'مطابقة' to express correspondence.
2
Understand the definition of truthfulness
Truthfulness means that everything the messenger reports about rulings, reward, punishment, etc., matches reality. This is a necessary attribute for messengers.
3
Examine the proof: miracles as verification
The proof is that God confirms the messenger by granting miracles. These miracles serve as God's statement that the messenger is truthful. The author likens it to God saying 'My servant has spoken the truth.'
This is a logical argument: since only God can produce miracles, they are a clear sign of divine approval.
4
Reflect on the connection to faith
This attribute is foundational because belief in the messenger's truthfulness is part of faith. Without it, the entire message would be undermined.
This leads to the next lesson on the two parts of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في النبوات
وأما الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فيجب لهم الصدقُ ؛ أي : مطابقةُ كلُّ ما أخبروا بهِ مِنْ أحكام وثواب وعقاب وغيرِها لِمَا في نفس الأمر ؛ لأنَّ الله تعالى قد صدقهم بما تَنزَّلَ مِنَ المعجز الذي خصهم الله به منزلة قولِهِ تعالى : صدق عبدي في كلَّ ما يُبلِّغُ عنِّي
هذا هو الجزء الثاني من جزأي الإيمانِ ؛ لأنَّ الإيمانَ مُركَّبٌ مِنْ جزأين : أحدهما : الإيمان بالله تعالى ؛ وهو حديث النفس التابع للمعرفة بما يجب له تعالى وما يستحيل وما يجوزُ
الثاني : الإيمان بالرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : وهو أيضاً حديث النفس التابع للمعرفة بما يجب لهم وما يستحيل وما يجوزُ
ولمَّا كانَ الجزء الثاني موقوفاً على الجزء الأولِ ؛ إِنَّما يُعرَفُ ويحصل بعد معرفتِهِ .. قَدَّمَ علماؤنا الكلام على الجزء الأول قبل الكلام على الجزء الثاني .
Speech on prophethood. As for the messengers, peace and blessings upon them, truthfulness is obligatory for them; that is, the conformity of everything they report of rulings, reward, punishment, and other matters to what is in reality; because God almighty has verified them by the miracle that descended, which God has specially given them, in the position of His saying: 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' This is the second of the two parts of faith; because faith is composed of two parts: one of them is faith in God almighty; and it is a discourse of the self following the knowledge of what is obligatory for Him, what is impossible for Him, and what is permissible for Him. The second is faith in the messengers, peace and blessings upon them; and it is also a discourse of the self following the knowledge of what is obligatory for them, what is impossible for them, and what is permissible for them. And since the second part is dependent on the first part, it is only known and obtained after knowledge of it, our scholars have presented speech on the first part before speech on the second part.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on prophethood (النبوات). It first defines a necessary attribute for messengers: truthfulness (الصدق). Truthfulness means that everything they report—rulings, reward, punishment, etc.—must correspond to reality. The proof for this is that God confirms them through miracles (المعجز) that He grants them. These miracles serve as God's verification, equivalent to His saying, 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' Next, the author explains that belief in the messengers constitutes the second of two parts of faith (الإيمان). Faith is composed of two parts: 1) faith in God, which is an inner conviction (حديث النفس) based on knowledge of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for Him; and 2) faith in the messengers, also an inner conviction based on knowledge of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for them. The second part depends on the first, so scholars traditionally discuss the first part before the second.

Correction: The passage establishes truthfulness as an obligatory attribute, proven by the miracles that God grants them, making lying impossible.

A) Their moral character
B) The miracles God grants them
