The Two Parts of Faith and Their Order
Explains the two parts of faith and their order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith is composed of two parts—belief in God and belief in His messengers—and why the part concerning God is discussed first.

Core Idea
Faith has two inseparable parts: belief in God and belief in His messengers.

After establishing the necessity of truthfulness for messengers, Sanusi now explains that belief in the messengers is the second component of faith. He defines both parts of faith and explains the logical order in which they are studied. This lesson clarifies that faith in God is the foundation for faith in the messengers.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'هذا هو الجزء الثاني' to the end. Notice how the author defines the two parts of faith.
2
Identify the two parts of faith
The first part is faith in God, which is an inner conviction based on knowledge of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for Him. The second part is faith in the messengers, also an inner conviction based on knowledge of their attributes.
Both are described as 'حديث النفس' (discourse of the self).
3
Understand the dependency
The second part depends on the first because one can only believe in messengers after knowing God. Thus, scholars discuss God's attributes before discussing the messengers.
This is a logical and pedagogical order.
4
Appreciate the scope
Faith involves not just belief in existence but also detailed knowledge of what is necessary, impossible, and possible for God and for messengers.
This sets the stage for the entire study of theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في النبوات
وأما الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فيجب لهم الصدقُ ؛ أي : مطابقةُ كلُّ ما أخبروا بهِ مِنْ أحكام وثواب وعقاب وغيرِها لِمَا في نفس الأمر ؛ لأنَّ الله تعالى قد صدقهم بما تَنزَّلَ مِنَ المعجز الذي خصهم الله به منزلة قولِهِ تعالى : صدق عبدي في كلَّ ما يُبلِّغُ عنِّي
هذا هو الجزء الثاني من جزأي الإيمانِ ؛ لأنَّ الإيمانَ مُركَّبٌ مِنْ جزأين : أحدهما : الإيمان بالله تعالى ؛ وهو حديث النفس التابع للمعرفة بما يجب له تعالى وما يستحيل وما يجوزُ
الثاني : الإيمان بالرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : وهو أيضاً حديث النفس التابع للمعرفة بما يجب لهم وما يستحيل وما يجوزُ
ولمَّا كانَ الجزء الثاني موقوفاً على الجزء الأولِ ؛ إِنَّما يُعرَفُ ويحصل بعد معرفتِهِ .. قَدَّمَ علماؤنا الكلام على الجزء الأول قبل الكلام على الجزء الثاني .
Speech on prophethood. As for the messengers, peace and blessings upon them, truthfulness is obligatory for them; that is, the conformity of everything they report of rulings, reward, punishment, and other matters to what is in reality; because God almighty has verified them by the miracle that descended, which God has specially given them, in the position of His saying: 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' This is the second of the two parts of faith; because faith is composed of two parts: one of them is faith in God almighty; and it is a discourse of the self following the knowledge of what is obligatory for Him, what is impossible for Him, and what is permissible for Him. The second is faith in the messengers, peace and blessings upon them; and it is also a discourse of the self following the knowledge of what is obligatory for them, what is impossible for them, and what is permissible for them. And since the second part is dependent on the first part, it is only known and obtained after knowledge of it, our scholars have presented speech on the first part before speech on the second part.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on prophethood (النبوات). It first defines a necessary attribute for messengers: truthfulness (الصدق). Truthfulness means that everything they report—rulings, reward, punishment, etc.—must correspond to reality. The proof for this is that God confirms them through miracles (المعجز) that He grants them. These miracles serve as God's verification, equivalent to His saying, 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' Next, the author explains that belief in the messengers constitutes the second of two parts of faith (الإيمان). Faith is composed of two parts: 1) faith in God, which is an inner conviction (حديث النفس) based on knowledge of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for Him; and 2) faith in the messengers, also an inner conviction based on knowledge of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for them. The second part depends on the first, so scholars traditionally discuss the first part before the second.

The Two Parts of Faith
Sanusi enumerates the two parts of faith and their dependency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith (iman) consists of two essential parts: belief in Allah and belief in His messengers, and why scholars discuss Allah's attributes first.

Core Idea
Faith has two inseparable parts: knowing Allah and knowing His messengers.

Sanusi introduces the structure of faith as a foundation for understanding prophethood. He explains that faith is not a simple concept but composed of two interrelated components. This passage clarifies the relationship between belief in Allah and belief in the messengers, and the logical order for studying them.

Guided Path

2

Discourse on prophethood. As for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: truthfulness is obligatory for them; i.e., the correspondence of everything they inform of, from rulings, reward, punishment, and other things, to what is in reality; because Allah the Exalted has confirmed them by the miracles that descended, which Allah has singled them out with, in the capacity of His saying: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me.' And since the second part depends on the first part, and is only known and attained after knowledge of it, our scholars presented the discourse on the first part before the discourse on the second part.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a combined explanation of the two parts of faith and a proof for the necessity of truthfulness in messengers. Sanusi begins by stating the topic: prophethood. He then asserts that truthfulness (ṣidq) is obligatory for messengers, defining it as the correspondence of all their reports (rulings, reward, punishment, etc.) to reality. The proof for this is that Allah has confirmed them through miracles, treating that confirmation as equivalent to His statement: 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' Next, he explains that faith (īmān) consists of two parts: belief in Allah (based on knowledge of His necessary, impossible, and possible attributes) and belief in the messengers (based on knowledge of their necessary, impossible, and possible attributes). The second part depends on the first, so scholars discuss God's attributes before discussing prophethood.

Key Takeaway

Why Messengers Must Be Truthful
Sanusi states the necessity of truthfulness for messengers and provides a proof from miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's stamp of approval on a messenger's truthfulness.

In this passage, Sanusi establishes one of the essential attributes of prophets: truthfulness. He not only defines it but provides a proof based on the miracles that accompany prophethood. This connects directly to the nature of faith in messengers.

Definition of a Messenger and His Conditions
Sanusi defines a messenger and discusses conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a messenger in Islamic theology and the scholarly debate about whether a messenger must bring a new law or book.

Core Idea
A messenger is a human sent by Allah with rulings, but a new law is not always required.

Sanusi begins by defining what a messenger is—a human being sent by Allah to convey His rulings. He then raises a key theological question: does a messenger always bring a new law or book? This passage sets the stage for understanding the prophetic office and its necessary attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic definition of a messenger carefully. Notice it specifies a human being sent to both male and female servants to convey two types of rulings.
The definition is foundational for all later discussions.
2
Identify the debated conditions
Sanusi lists three possible conditions for a messenger: bringing a new law, a specific book, or abrogating a previous law. He then notes there are scholarly opinions on whether any is required.
This is a point of scholarly disagreement.
3
Understand the obligation to know
He then states that we are obligated to know the messengers, and faith is not complete without knowing what is necessary, impossible, and possible for them.
This introduces the three categories used in prophetic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرُّسُلُ : جمع رسول ؛ وهو إنسان بعثَهُ الله سبحانَهُ إلى عبيدِهِ وإمائِهِ ليبلغهم عنه أحكامه التكليفيَّة والوضعية ، وما يتبعهما مِنْ وعدٍ ووعيد ونحوهما (١) .
وهل شرطه : أنْ يكونَ لهُ شرعٌ جديد ، أو كتاب مخصوص ، أو نسخ لشرع مَنْ قبلَهُ ، أو لا يُشترَطُ فِيهِ شَيْءٌ مِنْ ذلكَ ؟ أقوال . ونحنُ مُكلَّفونَ بمعرفةِ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا يَتِمُّ إيماننا إلا بذلك ، ولا يحصلُ لنا الإيمان إلا بمعرفة ما يجب لهم وما يستحيلُ وما يجوزُ
And the messengers (ar-rusul) is the plural of messenger (rasūl); and he is a human being whom Allah—glory be to Him—sent to His male and female servants to convey to them from Him His rulings: the prescriptive (taklīfiyya) and the declaratory (waḍ‘iyya), and what follows them from promise, threat, and the like of them (1). And is its condition that he has a new law, or a specific book, or an abrogation of the law of those before him, or is nothing of that required? [There are] statements. And we are obligated to know the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and our faith is not complete except by that, and we do not attain faith except by knowledge of what is necessary for them, what is impossible, and what is possible.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the term 'messenger' (rasūl) followed by a discussion of its conditions. Sanusi states that a messenger is a human being sent by Allah to His servants (both male and female) to convey from Him two types of rulings: prescriptive (taklīfiyya, e.g., commands and prohibitions) and declaratory (waḍ‘iyya, e.g., conditions and causes), along with what accompanies them like promises of reward and threats of punishment. He then raises a question about the conditions of a messenger: is it required that he bring a new law (shar‘ jadīd), a specific revealed book (kitāb makhṣūṣ), or an abrogation (naskh) of a previous law, or is none of this required? He notes that there are multiple scholarly opinions (aqwāl). Finally, he emphasizes that we are obligated (mukallafūn) to know the messengers, and our faith (īmān) is not complete without that knowledge—specifically, knowledge of what is necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and possible (jā’iz) for them.

أحكام تكليفية
أحكام وضعية
وعد ووعيد
شرع جديد
كتاب مخصوص
نسخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume every messenger must bring a new law and book.
Correction: Sanusi notes that this is a matter of scholarly debate, not a settled condition.

Checkpoint

C) Knowing what is necessary, impossible, and possible for them.
D) Knowing their lineage and names.

Key Takeaway
A messenger is a human sent with divine rulings, but whether a new law is required is debated; true faith demands knowing their necessary, impossible, and possible attributes.

The Obligatory Attribute of Truthfulness for Messengers
Sanusi elaborates on the necessity and scope of truthfulness for messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that messengers are obligated to be truthful in everything they convey from Allah, and that falsehood is impossible from them both intentionally and unintentionally according to verified scholars.

Core Idea
Falsehood can never come from a messenger, not even by mistake.

Sanusi now turns to the attributes obligatory for messengers, beginning with truthfulness. This attribute is fundamental because the entire message depends on its accurate transmission. The passage clarifies that this truthfulness covers all reports from Allah, excluding any possibility of falsehood, whether deliberate or accidental.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text once to get a feel for Sanusi's style, then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا عمداً إجماعاً، ولا سهواً عند المحققين'.
2
Identify the definition of truthfulness
Notice how Sanusi defines truthfulness: their reports are only in accordance with reality. This is the core meaning.
3
Note the two levels of impossibility
Sanusi specifies that falsehood cannot occur intentionally (by consensus) or forgetfully (according to verified scholars). This is a stronger claim than some might think.
The phrase 'عند المحققين' limits the forgetfulness point to verified scholars.
4
Understand the consensus and scholarly view
Consider why intentional falsehood is impossible by consensus, and why some scholars extend this to forgetfulness. Reflect on the implications for prophecy.
5
Connect the footnote about reward and punishment
The footnote ties back to earlier discussion: promise leads to reward, threat to punishment, and the permissible results in neither. This clarifies the types of divine statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواجبات في حق الرسل الكرام عليهم الصلاة والسلام
[ صفةُ الصِّدْقِ لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وبرهانها ] فمما يجبُ لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : الصدقُ في كلَّ ما يُبلِّغونَ عن المولى تبارك وتعالى ؛ أي : لا يكون خبرهم في ذلك إلا مطابقاً لِمَا في نفس الأمر ، ولا يقعُ منهمُ الكذبُ في شيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ لا عمداً إجماعاً ، ولا سهواً عند المحققين
(١) يترتب على الوعدِ : الثوابُ ، وعلى الوعيدِ : العقاب ، وعلى المعبر عنه بقوله : ( ونحوهما ) وهو المباح : عدم الثواب والعقاب
The obligations regarding the noble messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. [The attribute of truthfulness for them, peace and blessings be upon them, and its proof.] Among what is obligatory for them, peace and blessings be upon them: truthfulness in everything they convey from the Master, Blessed and Exalted; i.e., their reports in that regard are only in accordance with what is in reality, and falsehood does not occur from them in any of that, neither intentionally—by consensus—nor forgetfully, according to the verified scholars. (1) Upon the promise follows reward, and upon the threat follows punishment, and upon that which is expressed by his saying 'and the like of them'—which is the permissible (mubāḥ)—follows the absence of reward and punishment.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a detailed clarification of the obligatory attribute of truthfulness (ṣidq) for messengers, with a proof and a nuance. Sanusi begins a new section on the obligations (wājibāt) regarding the noble messengers. He lists among those obligations: truthfulness in everything they convey from Allah. He defines truthfulness as their reports being in complete accordance with reality. Then he makes a precise claim: falsehood does not occur from them at all—neither intentionally (bi-‘amdan) by scholarly consensus (ijmā‘an), nor even forgetfully (sahwan) according to the verified scholars (muḥaqqiqīn). This excludes any possibility of error in their conveyance, even unintentional. The footnote clarifies that the earlier mention of 'promise, threat, and the like' refers to reward for promise, punishment for threat, and for the permissible (mubāḥ) there is neither reward nor punishment.

Key Terms
الصدق
عمداً
سهواً
المحققين
إجماعاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think messengers could unintentionally make mistakes in conveying revelation.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that according to verified scholars, even forgetful falsehood is impossible for messengers.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, in what manner is falsehood impossible from messengers?
A) Only intentionally, but forgetfulness may occur.
B) Neither intentionally nor forgetfully, according to verified scholars.
C) Only in matters of religion, not in worldly affairs.
D) Only when they are conveying rulings, not other statements.

Key Takeaway
Messengers are infallible in conveying revelation; falsehood cannot occur in their reports even unintentionally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse of the Quran or a hadith that challenges your desires or worldview, do you ever find yourself wishing it were different? This lesson declares that every report from the messenger is exactly as it is in reality—no mistakes, no exaggerations. Where in your heart is there resistance to fully submitting to that truth? What would it cost you to surrender that resistance today?
?
The prophets conveyed warnings of punishment and promises of reward with absolute sincerity. Have you ever treated the threat of Hell or the promise of Paradise as if they were mere metaphors or hyperbole? How does knowing that the messenger could not even unintentionally exaggerate change the weight you give to those words? Will you let that shift how you live in the next 24 hours?
?
You believe that the Prophet ﷺ never lied intentionally. But do you live as if he could have made a mistake in transmitting the Quran or Sunnah? For example, when you come across a ruling that is difficult to practice, do you subconsciously suspect it might not be exactly what Allah intended? How would your actions change if you were completely convinced that every word he spoke in revelation is exactly what Allah wanted you to hear—no errors, no forgetfulness?

Truthfulness is Obligatory for Messengers
Sanusi states the obligation of truthfulness for messengers and defines it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that truthfulness in conveying revelation is an essential attribute of messengers and that lying is impossible for them, even inadvertently.

Core Idea
A messenger cannot lie about God, not even by mistake.

Before Sanusi provides the proof, he first establishes the definition and scope of prophetic truthfulness. This lesson anchors the foundational attribute that all messengers share: absolute reliability in conveying Allah's message. We will see what this means and how it excludes both intentional and accidental falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the declaration of obligation
Read the Arabic sentence that states truthfulness is obligatory for messengers. Note the precise definition that follows.
2
Identify what is excluded
Notice that both intentional and inadvertent lying are excluded. The consensus covers intentional, and the investigators add inadvertent.
This shows the high level of prophetic protection (عصمة).
3
Connect to the next lesson
This definition sets the stage for the proof. The proof explains why lying is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواجبات في حق الرسل الكرام عليهم الصلاة والسلام
[ صفة الصدق لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وبرهانها ]
فمما يجب لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : الصدق في كل ما يبلغون عن المولى تبارك وتعالى ؛ أي : لا يكون خبرهم في ذلك إلا مطابقا لما في نفس الأمر ، ولا يقع منهم الكذب في شيء من ذلك لا عمدا إجماعا ، ولا سهوا عند المحققين .
وبرهان ذلك : أنه لو وقع الكذب في شيء مما بلغه الرسول عن الله تعالى .. لزم أن يسري ذلك الكذب إلى خبره تعالى ؛ لأنه تبارك وتعالى أشار إلى تصديق الرسول بفعل أوجده خارقا للعادة ، تحدى به الرسول – أي : ادعاه – قبل وقوعه ، وطلبه من المولى تبارك وتعالى بمثل [؟] دليلا على صدقه في كل ما يبلغ عنه ، فأوجده تبارك وتعالى له على وفق دعواه ، وأعجز سبحانه كل من يقصد تكذيبه ومعارضته أن يأتي ذلك الخارق ، فتنزل هذا الفعل من المولى تبارك وتعالى باعتبار الوضع أو العادة وقرينة الحال .. منزلة التصريح في الكلام بصدق رسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ بحيث لا يجد الموفق فرقا بين تصديق الله تعالى لرسله بهذا الفعل الموصوف بما سبق تصديقهم بكلامه الصريح .
ألا ترى أن ملكا من الملوك لو جمع في بعض الأوقات أهل مملكته، وقام من المجلس بعض عبيده بمرأى منه وقال ومسمع للناس : إن الملك قد بعثني إليكم بكذا وكذا، وينهاكم عن كذا وكذا، وها هو عالم بمقالتي هذه إليكم، سميع بصير، قادر على إهلاكي إن كذبت عنه، وآية صدقي فيما ادعيت عليه : أن أطلب منه أن يصدقني؛ بأن يفعل كذا وكذا مما لم تجر عادته أن يفعله، وأن يخصني بذلك، ولا يفعله لأحد ممن يقصد معارضتي وتكذيبي
The Obligations Regarding the Noble Messengers, peace and blessings be upon them
[ The Attribute of Truthfulness for them, peace and blessings be upon them, and its Proof ]
So among that which is obligatory for them, peace and blessings be upon them, is truthfulness in everything they convey from the Lord, blessed and exalted; that is: their report in that is only in accordance with what is in reality, and lying does not occur from them in anything of that, neither intentionally by consensus, nor inadvertently according to the investigators.
And the proof of that is: if lying occurred in something that the messenger conveyed from God, exalted be He, then it would necessarily follow that that lying would extend to His report, exalted be He; because He, blessed and exalted, indicated the confirmation of the messenger by an act He brought into existence which breaks the norm, with which the messenger challenged – that is, he claimed it – before its occurrence, and he requested it from the Lord, blessed and exalted, like [؟] as evidence of his truthfulness in everything he conveys from Him, so He, blessed and exalted, brought it into existence for him in accordance with his claim, and He, exalted be He, incapacitated everyone who intends to disbelieve him and oppose him from producing that miraculous act. So this act from the Lord, blessed and exalted, came down, by virtue of convention or custom and the contextual indication, to the status of explicit statement in speech regarding the truthfulness of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them; such that the one granted success finds no difference between God's confirmation of His messengers by this act described above and their confirmation by His explicit speech.
Do you not see that if a king among kings gathered at some time the people of his kingdom, and some of his slaves stood up from the assembly in his sight and said in the hearing of the people: 'The king has sent me to you with such and such, and forbids you from such and such', and he knows of this statement of mine to you, hearing, seeing, able to destroy me if I lie about him, and the sign of my truthfulness in what I claim upon him is that I ask him to confirm me by doing such and such which is not his habit to do, and to single me out with that, and not to do it for anyone who intends to oppose me and disbelieve me...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a proof (برهان) for the necessity of truthfulness in messengers. It begins by stating that truthfulness is obligatory for them in all they convey from God, meaning their reports must correspond to reality; lying is impossible, both intentionally and inadvertently according to the investigators. The proof then follows: if a messenger were to lie in anything he conveys from God, that lie would necessarily extend to God’s own report, because God confirms the messenger by performing a miraculous act (خارق للعادة) that the messenger challenges with before its occurrence. This act serves as evidence of the messenger’s truthfulness in all he conveys. God creates the miracle as claimed and incapacitates others from producing the like. By convention (وضع) or custom (عادة) and contextual indication (قرينة الحال), this miraculous act is equivalent to an explicit statement from God confirming the messenger’s truthfulness. The passage then presents an analogy: a king before his subjects, where a slave claims to be sent, and the king confirms him by performing an extraordinary act exclusively for that slave, demonstrating the validity of the analogy. The proof concludes that there is no difference between this type of confirmation and explicit verbal confirmation.

Key Terms
صدق
رسول
عمدا
سهوا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets might make honest mistakes when conveying revelation.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that even inadvertent error (سهو) is not possible for them according to the investigators.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what types of lying are impossible for messengers in conveying from God?
A) Only intentional lying is impossible
B) Both intentional and inadvertent lying are impossible
C) Only inadvertent lying is impossible
D) Lying is possible but they never do it

Key Takeaway
Messengers are absolutely truthful in conveying revelation, and even accidental misstatement is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even inadvertent error is impossible for the messengers, what does that demand of your trust in what they conveyed? Is there any part of the revelation you treat lightly because you suspect human error? How can you change that today?
?
The definition of truthfulness here is that the report corresponds to reality. When you speak about God, does your speech always correspond to what He has actually revealed, or do you add your own assumptions? Can you commit to checking every religious claim against the source?
?
Sanusi says lying does not occur from them in any of that. Does your certainty in the messengers' truthfulness reflect in your willingness to obey even when it is difficult? What is one command you have been resisting because your desires conflict with their truthful report?

The Proof of Truthfulness through Divine Confirmation
Sanusi presents the proof that truthfulness is necessary based on divine confirmation via miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles serve as divine confirmation of a messenger's truthfulness, forming a proof that lying is impossible.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's endorsement that a messenger is truthful.

After establishing that truthfulness is obligatory, Sanusi provides a rational proof grounded in the nature of miracles. This lesson unpacks that proof, showing how a miracle functions as an implicit declaration from God that the messenger is telling the truth. An analogy with a king's slave clarifies the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Read the Arabic from 'وبرهان ذلك' through the analogy. Try to understand the logical flow.
The proof is a conditional argument.
2
Analyze the conditional logic
If lying occurred, then the lie would be attributed to God because of the miracle. Since God cannot lie, the messenger cannot lie.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Examine the king analogy
The analogy illustrates how an extraordinary act by an authority figure serves as an implicit confirmation of a claim.
Note that the analogy is incomplete in the text.

Why Prophets Cannot Lie: The Miracle as Divine Attestation
Sanusi proves that prophets cannot lie by showing that a miracle is God's attestation, and a lie would imply God lying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that prophets cannot lie, based on the function of miracles as divine attestation and the impossibility of lying for God.

Core Idea
A miracle is God's explicit confirmation of a prophet's truthfulness.

Sanusi presents a rigorous proof that lying is impossible for prophets. He argues that the miracles granted to prophets function as God's direct statement of their truthfulness, so any lie would imply God is lying—which is impossible. Let's explore the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the royal analogy—it is the heart of the proof.
2
Identify the key claim and structure
Sanusi starts with a conditional: if a prophet lies, then God's news would be false. Trace how he establishes that the miracle is equivalent to an explicit statement from God.
3
Understand the royal analogy
The king's unusual act for a servant is understood as attesting his truthfulness. Similarly, God's miracle attests the prophet. Note that the act must be exclusive and challenging.
4
See how the conclusion follows
If the prophet lied, God would be attesting a liar, which is itself a lie. Since God cannot lie (His news accords with His knowledge), prophetic lying is impossible.
The impossibility of God lying is a separate argument from divine attributes.

وبرهان ذلكَ : أنَّهُ لو وقعَ الكذبُ في شيء مما بلغه الرسول عن الله تعالى .. لزمَ أنْ يسري ذلكَ الكذبُ إلى خبره تعالى ؛ لأنَّه تبارك وتعالى أشار إلى تصديقِ الرسولِ بفعل أوجَدَهُ خارقاً للعادة ، تحدى بهِ الرسول - أي : ادَّعاه - قبل وقوعِهِ ، وطلبَهُ مِنَ المولى تبارك وتعالى بمثل : سو دليلاً على صدقِهِ في كلِّ ما يُبلِّغُ عنهُ ، فأوجده تبارك وتعالى له على وَفْقِ دعواه ، وأعجزَ سبحانَهُ كلَّ مَنْ يقصد تكذيبه ومعارضتَهُ أنْ يأتيَ ذلك الخارقِ ، فَتَنزَّلَ هذا الفعلُ مِنَ المولى تبارك وتعالى باعتبارِ الوضع أو العادة وقرينة الحال.. منزلة التصريح في الكلامِ بصدْقِ رُسُلِهِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ بحيثُ لا يجد الموفَّقُ فَرْقاً بينَ تصديق الله تعالى لرسله بهذا الفعل الموصوف بما سبق تصديقهم بكلامه الصريح وبين ألا ترى أنَّ مَلِكاً مِنَ الملوكِ لو جمع في بعض الأوقاتِ أهلَ مملكتِهِ ، وقامَ مِنَ المجلس بعضُ عبيده بمرأى منه وقال ومسمع للناس : إنَّ الملك قد بعثني إليكم بكذا وكذا ، وينهـاكـم عـن كذا وكذا (١) ، وها هو عالم بمقالتي هذه إليكم ، سميع بصير ، قادر على إهلاكي إن كذبتُ عنه ، وآيةُ صدقي فيما ادعيتُ عليهِ : أنْ أطلب منه أن يُصدِّقني ؛ بأن يفعل كذا وكذا ممَّا لم تجر عادته أن يفعله ، وأن يخصني بذلك ، ولا يفعلهُ لأحدٍ ممَّنْ يقصد معارضتي وتكذيبي ثمَّ طلبَ مِنَ الملكِ ذلكَ الفعلَ ، ففعلهُ لهُ على وَفْق ما طلبه منه ، وخصه به دونَ غيرِهِ ممَّنْ يَقصِدُ معارضته والقدح في صدقِهِ ، فيُعلَمُ على الضَّرورة أنَّ الملك قد صَدَّقَهُ ، وأنَّ ذلك الفعل مِنَ الملكِ نازل في الدلالة على صدقِ ذلك المدَّعي منزلة صريح قول الملك : إنه قد صَدَقَ فيما يُبلغ عنِّي ، لا فرق بينهما أصلاً استحالةُ الكذب في خبرِهِ سبحانَهُ وإذا ثبت ذلكَ : لزمَ مِنْ كذب الرسول كذبُ الملكِ الذي صدَّقَهُ لأنَّ تصديق الكاذب كذبٌ ، ولمَّا كانَ الكذب على المولى تبارك وتعالى مستحيلاً ؛ لأنَّ خبرَهُ على وَفْقِ علمه جل وعلا(۱) ، والعلم لا يحتمل النقيض بوجه ، فالكلامُ التابع له كذلك .. لزمَ أنْ يكونَ الكذبُ في حقٌّ رسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام مستحيلاً ، وذلك ظاهر ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق . (۱) عُلِّقَ في ( د ) : ( بيانها مركب ؛ تقول : الإله خبره على وفق علمه ؛ لعدم التركيب في ذاته ، والخبرُ على وفق العلم لا يكون إلا صدقاً ، بيانه : قول الشيخ : العلم لا يحتمل النقيض ) ومعنى قوله هنا : ( لعدم التركيب في ذاته ( يعني : لا يُتصوَّرُ الكلام الحرفي المركب من الحروف ، فكلامه هو على حسب علمه من حيث الدلالة ، ويستحيل الخُلف في العلم ؛ لأنه ينقلب جهلاً ، فكذا الكلام .
And the proof of that is that if lying occurred in something that the messenger conveyed from God Almighty, then that lying would necessarily spread to the news of Him Almighty; because He, Blessed and Exalted, indicated the attestation of the messenger by an act He created, miraculous, with which the messenger challenged — i.e., he claimed it — before its occurrence, and requested it from the Lord Blessed and Exalted as something like evidence for his truthfulness in everything he conveys from Him. So He, Blessed and Exalted, brought it into existence for him in accordance with his claim, and He, Glorified, incapacitated everyone who intends to deny him and oppose him from producing that miracle. So this act became from the Lord Blessed and Exalted, by consideration of convention or custom and the context of the situation, in the position of explicit statement in speech of the truthfulness of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them; such that the successful person finds no difference between God Almighty's attestation of His messengers by this act described with what preceded, and their attestation by His explicit speech. Do you not see that if a king among kings gathered at some time the people of his kingdom, and some of his servants stood up from the assembly in his sight and said within earshot of the people: 'The king has sent me to you with such-and-such, and forbids you from such-and-such (1), and he is aware of this statement of mine to you, hearing, seeing, able to destroy me if I lie about him, and the sign of my truthfulness in what I claim against him is that I ask him to attest me by doing such-and-such which is not his custom to do, and that he distinguishes me with it, and does not do it for anyone who intends to oppose me and deny me.' Then he requested that act from the king, and he did it for him in accordance with what he requested from him, and distinguished him with it to the exclusion of others who intend to oppose him and impugn his truthfulness. So it is known necessarily that the king has attested him, and that that act from the king is in indicating the truthfulness of that claimant in the position of the king's explicit statement: 'He has spoken truthfully in what he conveys from me'; there is no difference between them at all. [Heading:] The impossibility of lying in His news, Glorified be He. And if that is established, then from the messenger's lying would follow the lying of the king who attested him, because attesting a liar is a lie. And since lying upon the Lord Blessed and Exalted is impossible — because His news is in accordance with His knowledge, Glorious and High (1), and knowledge does not admit contradiction in any way, and speech that follows it is likewise — then it necessarily follows that lying with respect to His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, is impossible. And that is apparent. And with God Almighty is success. (1) It was commented in (D): 'Its explanation is composite; you say: The deity's news is in accordance with His knowledge because of the lack of composition in His essence, and news that is in accordance with knowledge is nothing but truth. Its explanation: The shaykh's saying: Knowledge does not admit contradiction.' And the meaning of his statement here: 'because of the lack of composition in His essence' means: literal speech composed of letters is inconceivable; so His speech is according to His knowledge in terms of indication, and discrepancy in knowledge is impossible because it would turn into ignorance, and so likewise speech.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a logical proof demonstrating the impossibility of lying in prophets. The author, Sanusi, begins by stating the proposition: if a prophet were to lie in anything he conveys from God, that lie would entail God lying as well. The reason is that God supports the prophet with a miracle — an act that breaks natural custom — which serves as a divine attestation of the prophet's truthfulness in everything he reports. The miracle is brought about in accordance with the prophet's claim and incapacitates all who would challenge it. Therefore, the miracle functions like an explicit statement from God saying, 'My messenger is truthful.' To illustrate this, Sanusi presents a royal analogy: a servant stands before a king and his subjects, claiming the king sent him with a message, and offers a test — he asks the king to perform an unusual act for him and for no one else. When the king does exactly that, everyone knows necessarily that the king has attested the servant's truthfulness; the act is equivalent to a clear statement of confirmation. Similarly, when God performs a miracle at the request of a prophet, it is a decisive confirmation that the prophet is truthful. Next, Sanusi draws the conclusion: if a prophet lied, that would mean God (who attests him) is a liar, because attesting a liar is itself a lie. But lying is impossible for God because His news conforms to His knowledge, and knowledge cannot be contradictory. Since God's speech follows His knowledge, it must always be true. Therefore, lying by prophets is impossible. The passage ends with an explanatory note clarifying why God's speech cannot be composed of letters (as human speech is) but rather is according to His knowledge, and any discrepancy in knowledge would turn it into ignorance — so God's speech is necessarily truthful.

Correction: Sanusi clarifies that miracles are functionally equivalent to God's explicit statement confirming the prophet's veracity.

Checkpoint

B) That a king's unusual act for a specific person is equivalent to a clear statement of confirmation
C) That prophets must perform miracles to prove their sincerity
D) That custom and convention determine the meaning of actions

Key Takeaway
Miracles are not mere signs; they are God's explicit verification of a prophet's truthfulness, making prophetic lying logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The proof shows that if a prophet lied, God would be a liar. How does this realization affect the weight you give to the Prophet's commands in your daily life? Is there a specific command you have been neglecting that you will now treat as God's own directive?
?
You claim to believe that Muhammad is truthful—but does your heart feel the same certainty as if you heard God say, 'This man is truthful'? What would change in your priorities if you truly internalized that every sunnah is backed by divine attestation?

Proof of the Impossibility of Lying for Prophets
Sanusi proves the impossibility of lying for prophets with a logical argument and a clarifying gloss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that lying is impossible for prophets, grounded in Allah's truthfulness and the nature of His speech.

Core Idea
A prophet cannot lie because Allah would then be a liar.

Sanusi presents a concise but powerful proof that lying is impossible for prophets. The argument hinges on two premises: first, that Allah confirms the prophet through miracles, and second, that lying is impossible for Allah because His speech is identical to His knowledge. This lesson unpacks the logic and clarifies a subtle point about Allah's speech not being composed of letters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice the structure: a heading, a logical argument, and a gloss.
2
Understand the core argument
Trace the logic: if a prophet lied, then Allah (who confirms him) would be a liar. Since lying is impossible for Allah, it is impossible for prophets.
The key link is Allah's confirmation of the prophet through miracles.
3
Study the gloss on divine speech
The gloss explains why Allah's speech cannot be false: it is not composed of letters but is directly based on His knowledge, which cannot admit its opposite.
This reinforces the impossibility of lying for prophets.

استحالةُ الكذب في خبرِهِ سبحانَهُ ]
وإذا ثبت ذلك : لزمَ مِنْ كذب الرسول كذبُ الملكِ الذي صدَّقَهُ لأنَّ تصديق الكاذب كذبٌ ، ولمَّا كانَ الكذب على المولى تبارك وتعالى مستحيلاً ؛ لأنَّ خبرَهُ على وَفْقِ علمه جل وعلا(۱) ، والعلم لا يحتمل النقيض بوجه ، فالكلامُ التابع له كذلك .. لزمَ أنْ يكونَ الكذبُ في حقٌّ رسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام مستحيلاً ، وذلك ظاهر ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق .
(۱) عُلِّقَ في ( د ) : ( بيانها مركب ؛ تقول : الإله خبره على وفق علمه ؛ لعدم التركيب في ذاته ، والخبرُ على وفق العلم لا يكون إلا صدقاً ، بيانه : قول الشيخ : العلم لا يحتمل النقيض )
•
ومعنى قوله هنا : ( لعدم التركيب في ذاته ) يعني : لا يُتصوَّرُ الكلام الحرفي المركب من الحروف ، فكلامه هو على حسب علمه من حيث الدلالة ، ويستحيل الخُلف في العلم ؛ لأنه ينقلب جهلاً ، فكذا الكلام .
The impossibility of lying in His speech, glory be to Him.
And if that is established, then from the lying of the messenger follows the lying of the king who confirmed him, because confirming a liar is lying. And since lying against the Master, blessed and exalted, is impossible because His speech is in accordance with His knowledge, glory be to Him, and knowledge does not admit its opposite in any way, so speech which is dependent on it is likewise... it follows that lying on the part of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, is impossible. That is apparent, and with Allah Almighty is success.
(1) It was commented in (D): 'Its explanation is composite: you say: the divine's speech is in accordance with His knowledge, due to the absence of composition in His essence, and speech in accordance with knowledge is only true. Its explanation: the saying of the Shaykh: knowledge does not admit its opposite.' And the meaning of his saying here: 'due to the absence of composition in His essence' means: literal speech composed of letters is not conceivable, so His speech is according to His knowledge in terms of indication, and discrepancy in knowledge is impossible because it would turn into ignorance, so likewise speech.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the impossibility of lying for prophets. It begins by stating the heading: 'The impossibility of lying in His speech, glory be to Him.' Then it presents an argument: if a prophet were to lie, then the king (i.e., Allah) who confirmed him through miracles would be a liar, because confirming a liar is itself a lie. Since lying is impossible for Allah (because His speech is necessarily true, being based on His infallible knowledge), it follows that lying is also impossible for His messengers. The author then includes a gloss in which a commentator clarifies the reasoning: Allah's speech is not composed of letters (due to the absence of composition in His essence), so it is not like human speech. Rather, it is a conceptual indication that follows His knowledge. Since knowledge cannot be false, speech that is based on it cannot be false either. Thus, the impossibility of lying in Allah's speech entails the impossibility of lying in the prophets' reporting from Him.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Lying is impossible for prophets because it would implicate Allah in falsehood, which is impossible given His perfect knowledge and speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This passage shows the chain: doubting a prophet implicates Allah in falsehood. Where in your life have you treated prophetic reports as uncertain, and who does that really doubt?
?
The proof rests on Allah's speech being perfectly true. When you hear a command from the Quran or a hadith, do you immediately obey, or do you hesitate? Your hesitation, when examined, is a form of disbelief in the truthfulness of the reporting chain. How will you respond to this passage's demand for absolute trust?
?
The gloss removes any chance that Allah's speech could be like human speech — it is not composed of letters, so it cannot err. Does your heart still try to minimize Allah's word as something 'interpreted' or 'culturally conditioned'? Will you allow this truth to make you tremble at every verse, knowing it is from the One who cannot lie?

The Attribute of Trustworthiness for Prophets
Sanusi defines the prophetic attribute of trustworthiness and provides its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic attribute of trustworthiness (amānah), its definition, and its proof from the obligation to emulate the prophets.

Core Idea
Trustworthiness means leaving each action in its proper place as commanded by Allah.

Sanusi now turns to the second essential perfection of prophets: trustworthiness. He defines it not merely as honesty but as a comprehensive preservation of both external and internal states from anything forbidden or disliked. The proof is drawn from the fact that followers must imitate the prophets in all things, which necessitates the prophets' infallibility in those actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and proof
Read the passage and note how Sanusi defines trustworthiness as safeguarding from forbidden and disliked acts. Identify the proof based on imitation.
2
Understand the four categories
Examine how trustworthiness applies differently to obligatory/recommended acts versus forbidden/disliked acts, using the metaphor of 'chests of existence and non-existence'.
3
Reflect on the term 'infallibility'
Notice that the passage equates trustworthiness with 'infallibility' (ʿiṣmah). Consider why this connection is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة الأمانة لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وبرهانها ]
ويجب لهم الأمانة (۱) ، أي : حفظ ظواهرهم وبواطنهم مِنَ الوقوع في مُحرَّم أو مكروه ؛ لأنَّ أتباعهم أُمروا بالاقتداء بهم في جميع أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، وذلك يستلزم عصمتهم فيها مِنْ كُلِّ منهي عنه .
هذا كمال ثانٍ واجب للرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ وهو كونُهم أمناء ، لا خيانة لهم في شيءٍ مِنَ الأشياء ؛ والأمينُ : هو الذي يتركُ كل أمر على الوجه الذي أوصى مالكُهُ أنْ يُترَكَ عليهِ ، ولا يخونُ ؛ بأن ينقله بسبب الشهوةِ مِنَ الموضع الذي ينبغي أن يكون فيه بوصية مالكه الذي تجب طاعته .
فالأمانة في الواجب والمندوبِ : أَنْ يُدْخَلا في شريف صندوقِ الوجودِ ، كما أوصى بذلك فيهما مولانا جل وعزَّ ، ولا يُخان بنقلهما عنه إلى آفة العدم .
والأمانة في المُحرَّم والمكروه : أنْ يُدْخَلا في صندوقِ آفة العدمِ ، ولا يُنقلا عنه إلى شريف الوجودِ ، كما أوصى أيضاً بذلك فيهما مولانا تبارك وتعالى .
(۱) ويعبّر عنها بالعصمة أيضاً .
The attribute of trustworthiness for them, peace and blessings be upon them, and its proof.
And trustworthiness is obligatory for them (1), i.e., safeguarding their external and internal from falling into what is forbidden or disliked, because their followers are commanded to emulate them in all their sayings and actions, and that necessitates their infallibility from everything prohibited.
This is a second perfection obligatory for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: that they are trustworthy, no betrayal in anything. And the trustworthy one is he who leaves every matter in the manner that its owner commanded it to be left, and does not betray by moving it due to desire from the place it should be by the instruction of its owner whose obedience is obligatory.
So trustworthiness in the obligatory and recommended is that they be entered into the noble chest of existence, as our Master, mighty and majestic, commanded regarding them, and not be betrayed by moving them from it to the affliction of non-existence.
And trustworthiness in the forbidden and disliked is that they be entered into the chest of the affliction of non-existence, and not be moved from it to the noble existence, as our Master, blessed and exalted, also commanded regarding them.
(1) And it is also referred to as infallibility.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a proof establishing the attribute of trustworthiness (amānah) for the prophets. It begins by stating the heading, then explains its necessity: prophets must be trustworthy, meaning they are protected from falling into forbidden or disliked acts both externally and internally. The reason is that their followers are commanded to imitate them in all sayings and actions, which requires that the prophets be infallible (ʿiṣmah) in these matters. The author identifies this as the second essential perfection for prophets (after truthfulness). He then defines the 'trustworthy one' (al-amīn) as someone who leaves every matter exactly as its owner commanded it to be left, without betraying by moving it out of desire. This general definition is applied to four categories of actions: (1) For obligatory and recommended acts, trustworthiness means bringing them into existence (the 'noble chest of existence') as commanded, and not moving them to non-existence. (2) For forbidden and disliked acts, trustworthiness means keeping them in non-existence (the 'chest of affliction of non-existence') and not bringing them into existence. The metaphor of 'chests' illustrates that each type of action has a proper place, and the trustworthy person preserves that placement. The passage concludes with a note that this attribute is also called 'infallibility' (ʿiṣmah).

آفة العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think trustworthiness only applies to avoiding forbidden acts.
Correction: Trustworthiness also includes performing obligatory and recommended acts as commanded; it is about placing each action in its proper state.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does trustworthiness require regarding forbidden and disliked actions?
A) They should be brought into existence.
B) They should be kept in non-existence.
C) They should be changed to permissible acts.
D) They should be ignored.

Key Takeaway
Trustworthiness for prophets means preserving their actions in the proper state as commanded by Allah, ensuring they neither commit forbidden acts nor omit obligatory ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Prophet (peace be upon him), but ask yourself: in which area of your life are you moving a forbidden act from non-existence into existence because of your desire? What would it cost you to keep it in non-existence, and are you willing to pay that price?
?
The passage says trustworthiness means leaving every action exactly as its Owner commanded. Right now, which obligatory act are you neglecting—moving it from existence toward non-existence? What is stopping you from bringing it back into the 'noble chest of existence' today?
?
You trust the prophets completely, but do you trust Allah's commands enough to leave a disliked habit that you secretly cling to? What would it look like to truly entrust that matter to Allah by leaving it as He commanded?

The Prophets' Trustworthiness: Definition and Proof
Sanusi defines prophetic trustworthiness and gives a logical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of prophetic trustworthiness (al-amānah), its scope covering all actions, and the rational proof that prophets must be infallible.

Core Idea
Absolute emulation of prophets demands their complete infallibility.

Sanusi now turns to the second perfection of prophets: trustworthiness. He defines it as preserving God's instructions in all actions, and then provides a powerful rational argument: if a prophet could sin, his followers' duty to emulate him would make that sin permissible—an impossible contradiction. This lesson unpacks that definition and proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of trustworthiness
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice how Sanusi defines trustworthiness as preserving both outward and inward from forbidden and disliked acts.
The definition is grounded in the command to emulate the prophets absolutely.
2
Distinguish the two applications
The passage applies trustworthiness to obligatory/recommended acts (bringing them into existence) and forbidden/disliked acts (keeping them in non-existence). Identify this distinction.
3
Understand the logical proof
Follow the argument: because followers must emulate prophets absolutely, any sinful act by a prophet would gain implicit permission, contradicting its prohibition. This proves prophets cannot sin.
The proof uses the principle of jam‘ bayn al-naqīḍayn (conjunction of opposites).

صفة الأمانة لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وبرهانها ويجب لهم الأمانة (۱) ، أي : حفظ ظواهرهم وبواطنهم مِنَ الوقوع في مُحرَّم أو مكروه ؛ لأنَّ أتباعهم أُمروا بالاقتداء بهم في جميع أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، وذلك يستلزم عصمتهم فيها مِنْ كُلِّ منهي عنه هذا كمال ثانٍ واجب للرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ وهو كونُهم أمناء ، لا خيانة لهم في شيءٍ مِنَ الأشياء ؛ والأمينُ : هو الذي يتركُ كل أمر على الوجه الذي أوصى مالكُهُ أنْ يُترَكَ عليهِ ، ولا يخونُ ؛ بأن ينقله بسبب الشهوةِ مِنَ الموضع الذي ينبغي أن يكون فيه بوصية مالكه الذي تجب طاعته فالأمانة في الواجب والمندوبِ : أَنْ يُدْخَلا في شريف صندوقِ الوجودِ ، كما أوصى بذلك فيهما مولانا جل وعزَّ ، ولا يُخان بنقلهما عنه إلى آفة العدم والأمانة في المُحرَّم والمكروه : أنْ يُدْخَلا في صندوقِ آفة العدمِ ، ولا يُنقلا عنه إلى شريف الوجودِ ، كما أوصى أيضاً بذلك فيهما مولانا تبارك وتعالى (۱) ويعبّر عنها بالعصمة أيضاً. ولا شك أنَّ الأفعال والذواتِ كلَّها مُلْكُ لمولانا جل وعلا ، وقد أوصى سبحانه وتعالى فيها بوصايا وهي أحكامه الشرعيَّةُ ؛ فالأمانة : المحافظة على وصاياه جلَّ وعلا، وعدم التبديل فيها والتغيير . ولمَّا كانَ الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ أكرمَ الخلْقِ على الله ، وأتقاهم الله ، وأعرفهم بالله ، وأشدَّهم خوفاً منه . . كانوا أعظم الناسِ أمانةً ، وأشدَّهم محافظة على وصاياه تبارك وتعالى ولما أكرمهم سبحانه وتعالى بأعظم أمانة ، وعصمهم مِنْ كلّ خيانة.. جعلهم قدوةً لأُممهم ، وأطلق في متابعتهم ولم يجعل فيها تقييداً ، فلو جوزنا أن يقع في أفعالهم ما هو مُحرَّم أو مكروه .. لزم أن يجتمع في ذلك المحرَّمِ والمكروه : الإذنُ في فعلهما ؛ أخذاً مِنْ قاعدة الترغيبِ في متابعة الرسل والحضُّ على الاقتداء بهم وعدم الإذنِ لِمَا فُرِضَ فيهما مِنَ التحريم والكراهة ، وذلك جمع بين النقيضين .
The attribute of trustworthiness (al-amānah) for them, peace and blessings be upon them, and its proof: Trustworthiness is obligatory for them (1), i.e., the preservation of their outward and inward aspects from falling into what is forbidden (ḥarām) or disliked (makrūh); because their followers are commanded to emulate them in all their sayings and deeds, and that necessitates their infallibility ('iṣmah) in them from everything prohibited. This is a second perfection obligatory for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them; namely that they are trustworthy (umanā'), having no treachery in any thing. The trustworthy person (al-amīn) is the one who leaves every matter in the manner that its owner commanded it to be left, and does not betray by transferring it due to desire from the place where it ought to be according to the instruction of its owner whose obedience is obligatory. So trustworthiness regarding the obligatory (wājib) and recommended (mandūb) is that they should be entered into the noble chest of existence, as our Lord, Exalted and Glorified, commanded concerning them, and they should not be betrayed by transferring them from it to the calamity of non-existence. And trustworthiness regarding the forbidden (ḥarām) and disliked (makrūh) is that they should be entered into the chest of the calamity of non-existence, and they should not be transferred from it to the noble existence, as our Lord, Blessed and Exalted, also commanded concerning them. (1) And it is also called infallibility ('iṣmah). And there is no doubt that all actions and essences are the property of our Lord, Exalted and Glorified, and He, Glorious and Exalted, has given instructions (waṣāyā) concerning them; they are His legal rulings (aḥkāmuhu al-shar‘iyyah). So trustworthiness is the preservation of His instructions, Glorious and Exalted, and not altering or changing them. And since the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, are the most honored of creation by God, the most God-fearing, the most knowledgeable of God, and the most fearful of Him... they are the greatest of people in trustworthiness, and the most stringent in preserving His instructions, Blessed and Exalted. And since He, Glorious and Exalted, honored them with the greatest trustworthiness and protected them from every treachery... He made them models (qudwah) for their nations, and He made following them absolute with no restriction. Thus if we allowed that something forbidden or disliked could occur in their actions, then it would be necessary that in that forbidden and disliked there would be permission to do them, taken from the principle of encouraging the following of the messengers and urging emulation of them, while there is no permission for what has been prescribed to them of prohibition and dislike. And that is a conjunction of opposites (jam‘ bayn al-naqīḍayn).
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of trustworthiness (al-amānah) for the prophets, provides its proof, and explains its implications. It begins by stating that trustworthiness is obligatory for the prophets, defining it as the preservation of their outer and inner from falling into anything forbidden (ḥarām) or disliked (makrūh). The reason given is that their followers are commanded to emulate them in all sayings and deeds, which necessitates their infallibility (ʿiṣmah) from everything prohibited. The author then describes this as a second perfection for the prophets: they are trustworthy (umanāʾ), having no treachery. The definition of a trustworthy person is one who leaves every matter as its owner commanded, not betraying by moving it due to desire. The author then explains the application of trustworthiness to different types of actions: for obligatory and recommended acts, they must be placed into existence and not removed to non-existence; for forbidden and disliked acts, they must be placed into non-existence and not brought into existence. A footnote notes that this trustworthiness is also called infallibility (ʿiṣmah). The passage then expands by stating that all actions and essences belong to God, and He has given instructions (waṣāyā), i.e., His legal rulings. Trustworthiness is preserving these instructions. The proof for the prophets' trustworthiness is then given: because the prophets are the most honored, God-fearing, knowledgeable, and fearful of God, they are the most trustworthy. God made them models (qudwah) for their nations and commanded absolute following without restriction. If a prophet could commit a forbidden or disliked act, then that act would become permitted due to the command to follow, but it is inherently prohibited—this is a conjunction of opposites, which is impossible. Therefore, prophets must be protected from all forbidden and disliked actions.

Key Terms
أمانة (amānah)
عصمة (ʿiṣmah)
وصايا (waṣāyā)
قدوة (qudwah)
اقتداء (iqtidāʾ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are only protected from major sins.
Correction: The passage states they are protected from all forbidden and disliked actions, including minor sins and disliked acts.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would necessarily follow if a prophet committed a forbidden act?
A) The act would be expiated by repentance.
B) The act would become permissible due to the command to follow the prophet.
C) The prophet would lose his prophethood.
D) The act would be considered a mistake, not a sin.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be absolutely trustworthy (amānah), protected from all sin and disliked acts, because their followers are commanded to emulate them without restriction, making any sin in them logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In light of the definition that trustworthiness is preserving God's instructions without alteration, consider one area of your life where you have been 'transferring' what should exist (like a prayer) into non-existence (neglect). What is one specific change you will make today to restore that duty to God's 'noble chest of existence'?
?
The proof in this lesson shows that if a prophet could sin, it would cause a logical contradiction in God's law. How does this absolute trustworthiness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) confront your own justifications for compromising on sunnah practices in your daily life? Will you commit to following him in even the smallest matters, knowing that any gap in emulation reflects a gap in your trust in his example?
?
Think of a person in your life who looks up to you as a model (e.g., a child, younger sibling, or colleague). How does the lesson's argument about the necessity of trustworthiness for those who are models challenge you to reevaluate your own consistency in actions? What habit or attitude will you surrender to God today so that you become a more trustworthy reflection of prophetic character?

The Proof of Prophetic Delivery (Tabligh)
Sanusi proves that prophets delivered all they were commanded to deliver.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that prophets delivered every command they were given, based on their trustworthiness and the consensus of the early Muslims.

Core Idea
Prophets never withheld any command — proof lies in their trustworthiness and the consensus of the community.

Sanusi now turns to the attribute of tabligh (delivery). He establishes that prophets must have delivered everything commanded, leaving nothing out. This lesson explores the rational proof from trustworthiness and the traditional proof from consensus, along with Qur'anic confirmation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: statement first, then two proofs.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between intentional and forgetful omission. Find where Sanusi addresses each.
Intentional omission is handled first, then forgetfulness.
3
Understand the proof for each
For intentional: based on trustworthiness (amana). For forgetfulness: based on consensus (ijma). Read the commentary to see how each proof works.
4
Reflect on the Qur'anic evidence
Sanusi cites verse 5:3 from Al-Ma'idah. Consider how this verse supports the completeness of delivery.
The verse declares religion perfected and favor completed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب لهم أيضاً أنَّهم بلغوا كل ما أمرهم المولى سبحانه، بتبليغه، ولم يتركوا شيئاً منه، لا نسياناً ولا عمداً؛ أمَّا عمداً فلما سبق في الأمانة، وأما نسياناً فللإجماع هذا أيضاً كمال ثالث واجبٌ للرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام؛ وهو وفاؤهم بتبليغ كلّ ما أرسلَهمُ الله تعالى بهِ وأمرهم أَنْ يُبلغوه للناسِ، وأنَّهم لم يُخفُوا عنِ الناسِ شيئاً مِنْ ذلكَ، لا عمداً ولا نسياناً، والتبليغ في ذلك على الوجه الذي أمروا بهِ مِنْ عموم للناس أو خصوص لهم وبرهان امتناع إخفائهم شيئاً مِنْ ذلك على طريق العمدِ: واضحٌ مِنْ برهان الأمانةِ السابقِ؛ لأنَّ هذا كتمان للحقِّ وخيانة محرَّمةٌ، وهم أمناء معصومونَ مِنَ المحرَّم أن يُدخِلوهُ في دائرة الوجود بعد معرفتهم نهي مولانا جل وعلا عن ذلكَ وأما إخفاؤهم شيئاً مِنْ ذلك على طريق النسيان: فالمحققون أيضاً على منعه، ودليله: إجماع السلف وقد صَرَّحَ القرآنُ بكمال التبليغ في حق نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في قولِهِ تعالى: ﴿ الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي ﴾ [المائدة: ٣] وصرَّحَ أيضاً بذلك النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في الحديثِ ولم يحضرني الآن لفظ الحديث
And it is also obligatory for them that they delivered everything that the Lord, glorified be He, commanded them to deliver, and they did not leave anything from it, neither out of forgetfulness nor intentionally. As for intentionally, it is because of what preceded concerning trustworthiness (al-amāna). And as for forgetfully, it is due to consensus (al-ijmā'). This is also a third perfection obligatory for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: it is their fulfillment in delivering everything that Allah Almighty sent them with and commanded them to convey to the people, and that they did not conceal from the people anything of that, neither intentionally nor forgetfully. And the delivery in that is in the manner they were commanded, whether generally for all people or specifically for some. And the proof of the impossibility of their concealing anything of that intentionally is clear from the previous proof of trustworthiness; because this is concealment of truth and a forbidden betrayal, and they are trustworthy and infallible from bringing a forbidden thing into existence after their knowledge of the prohibition of our Lord, Exalted and Glorified, of that. As for their concealing anything of that forgetfully, the verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqūn) also forbid it, and its proof is the consensus of the early Muslims (ijmā' al-salaf). And the Qur'an has explicitly stated the perfection of delivery concerning our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in His statement, the Most High: 'This day I have perfected for you your religion and completed My favor upon you' [Al-Mā'idah 5:3]. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, also explicitly stated that in the hadith, but the wording of the hadith is not present to me now.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation of the prophetic attribute of tablīgh (delivery of the message). Sanusi begins by stating the obligation: prophets must have delivered everything they were commanded to deliver, omitting nothing, whether intentionally or forgetfully. He then provides separate proofs for each case. For intentional concealment, he argues from the previously established attribute of amāna (trustworthiness): hiding the message is a betrayal and forbidden, and prophets are infallible (ma‘ṣūm) from committing forbidden acts knowingly. For forgetfulness, he appeals to ijmā' (consensus) of the early Muslims (salaf) that prophets did not forget to deliver any part of the message. He supports this with the Qur’anic verse from Sūrat al-Mā’idah (5:3) which declares the completion of religion, implying that the Prophet delivered everything. Finally, he mentions a corroborating hadith without citing its exact wording. The passage follows a logical sequence: obligation statement, then proof, then scriptural evidence.

Key Terms
تبليغ
أمانة
عصمة
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets only had to deliver most of the message, not all of it.
Correction: Sanusi insists on completeness without any omission, intentional or forgetful, and provides proofs.

Checkpoint
What proof does Sanusi give for the impossibility of prophets intentionally hiding part of the message?
A) The consensus of the early Muslims
B) The previous proof of trustworthiness (amana)
C) The Qur'anic verse in Al-Ma'idah
D) The hadith of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Prophets perfectly delivered all they were commanded, proven by their infallibility from intentional betrayal and by the consensus of the salaf against forgetfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet delivered every command of Allah to the last detail, including those you find hardest to obey? Which command do you struggle with most, and how does acknowledging perfect tabligh challenge your selective obedience?
?
If the Prophet never withheld any part of the message out of fear or convenience, what does that say about your own willingness to speak the truth when it is difficult? In what area of your life are you tempted to conceal or soften the truth?
?
The proof of delivery rests on trustworthiness and infallibility. When you consider your own trustworthiness in conveying religious knowledge to others, do you ever omit or downplay parts that you find uncomfortable? How can the Prophet's example hold you accountable today?

Prophets Cannot Intentionally Conceal the Message
Sanusi gives a rational proof against intentional concealment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that prophets are trustworthy and cannot intentionally hide any part of the divine message.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from the act of hiding the truth.

Sanusi begins by establishing that intentionally concealing the message would be a betrayal, which is strictly forbidden. Since prophets are appointed as trustworthy conveyors, they are divinely protected from ever committing such an act. This lesson unpacks that foundational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without focusing on translation. Allow the rhythm and terms to sink in.
Notice the key terms: برهان الأمانة, كتمان, خيانة.
2
Understand the key terms
Identify الأمانة (trustworthiness) and how it relates to the prohibition of كتمان (concealment) and خيانة (betrayal).
These are central to the argument.
3
Follow the logical argument
The passage states: concealment is betrayal, which is forbidden. Prophets are trustworthy and protected from bringing any forbidden act into existence because they know Allah's prohibition. Therefore, they cannot conceal.
This is a straightforward deductive argument.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this attribute is essential for the credibility of prophethood. If a prophet could hide even a small part of revelation, the entire message would be unreliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان الأمانةِ السابقِ ؛ لأنَّ هذا كتمان للحقِّ وخيانة محرَّمةٌ ، وهم أمناء معصومونَ مِنَ المحرَّم أن يُدخِلوهُ في دائرة الوجود بعد معرفتهم نهي مولانا جل وعلا عن ذلكَ
وأما إخفاؤهم شيئاً مِنْ ذلك على طريق النسيان : فالمحققون (۱) أيضاً على منعه ، ودليله : إجماع السلف
وقد صَرَّحَ القرآنُ بكمال التبليغ في حق نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي ﴾ [المائدة : ٣]
وصرَّحَ أيضاً بذلك النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في الحديثِ (۲)
ولم يحضرني الآن لفظ الحديث (٢) .
وصرَّحَ بذلكَ الرُّسُلُ في القرآنِ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ( أُبَلِّغُكُمْ رِسَلَتِ ربي ﴾ [الأعراف : ٤٦٢] ، وقوله جلَّ وعلا: ﴿ لَقَدْ أَبْلَغْتُكُمْ رِسَالَةَ رَبِّي وَنَصَحْتُ لَكُمْ وَلَكِن لَّا تُحِبُّونَ النَّصِحِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ٧٩] ، وقوله تبارك وتعالى : ﴿ لَقَدْ أَبْلَغْتُكُمْ رِسَلَنتِ رَبِّي وَنَصَحْتُ لَكُمْ فَكَيْفَ وَاسَى عَلَى قَوْمٍ كَفِرِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ۹۳] وتتبع نحو ذلك في القرآن كثير(۱) ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق
The proof of the aforementioned trustworthiness: because this is concealment of truth and a forbidden betrayal, and they are trustworthy ones protected from introducing the forbidden into the realm of existence after their knowledge of the prohibition of our Master, Exalted and Glorified, of that. As for their concealing something of that by way of forgetfulness, the investigators (1) also hold its prohibition, and its proof is the consensus of the Salaf. And the Qur'an has explicitly stated the perfection of delivery regarding our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in His saying, Exalted is He: 'This day I have perfected for you your religion and completed upon you My favor' [al-Ma'idah 5:3]. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, also stated that in the hadith (2), and I do not have at hand now the wording of the hadith (2). And the messengers stated that in the Qur'an, such as His saying, Exalted is He: 'I convey to you the messages of my Lord' [al-A'raf 7:62], and His saying, Glorified and Exalted: 'I have conveyed to you the message of my Lord and advised you, but you do not like the advisors' [al-A'raf 7:79], and His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'I have conveyed to you the messages of my Lord and advised you; so how could I grieve over a disbelieving people?' [al-A'raf 7:93]. And similar to that is abundant in the Qur'an (1), and with Allah, Exalted, is success.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage contains a two-part proof for the infallibility of prophets in delivering the message. First, it argues that intentionally hiding the message is forbidden because it is a betrayal; prophets are trustworthy (أمناء) and protected from such. Second, it addresses the possibility of forgetfully omitting the message: the 'investigators' (المحققون) also forbid this, and the evidence is the consensus of the Salaf (إجماع السلف). The author then supports the perfection of delivery with explicit Qur'anic verses: the verse from al-Ma'idah shows the completion of religion for the Prophet Muhammad, and verses from al-A'raf (7:62, 79, 93) show the same for earlier prophets. The passage thus establishes that prophets must deliver the entire message without any omission, whether intentional or forgetful.

Key Terms
الأمانة
الكتمان
الخيانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is it impossible for a prophet to intentionally conceal the divine message?
A) Because they are physically unable to forget
B) Because it would be a betrayal and they are protected from such
C) Because they are afraid of punishment
D) Because they have no free will

Key Takeaway
Prophets are inherently trustworthy and protected from committing the forbidden act of concealing truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself omitting parts of Islamic teachings because you fear how others might react? How does the example of the prophets, who never concealed even the hardest truths, expose your excuse as a form of betrayal?
?
When you speak about your faith, are you selective, sharing only what is easy or popular? What would it mean for you to embody the amanah of the prophets by conveying the full message, regardless of personal cost?
?
Think of a specific time you withheld a truth to avoid discomfort or maintain a relationship. How does the knowledge that concealment is a forbidden betrayal (خيانة محرمة) stir your conscience, and what concrete step can you take today to repent and practice complete honesty?

Prophets Cannot Forget the Message
Sanusi proves that prophets cannot forget the message.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets are protected even from forgetfully omitting the divine message, based on consensus and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Even forgetfulness cannot cause a prophet to omit the message.

After establishing that intentional concealment is impossible, Sanusi addresses a subtler possibility: what if a prophet simply forgets to convey something? He asserts that this too is prohibited, relying on the consensus of the early scholars (إجماع السلف) and explicit Quranic affirmations that the message was delivered perfectly. This lesson examines those proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on forgetfulness
Read from 'وأما إخفاؤهم شيئاً من ذلك على طريق النسيان' to the end. Notice the structure: first the claim, then the proof (consensus), then supporting Quranic verses.
There are multiple Quranic verses cited.
2
Identify the main proof
The author states that the investigators (المحققون) hold the prohibition of forgetful omission, and the evidence is the consensus of the Salaf.
Consensus is considered a strong proof in Islamic theology.
3
Review the Quranic verses
Read the verses from al-Ma'idah 5:3 and al-A'raf 7:62,79,93. Each emphasizes that the prophets fully delivered the message.
Verse 5:3 speaks specifically of completion of religion for the Prophet Muhammad.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why would God allow a prophet to forget? Forgetfulness would introduce doubt about the completeness of the revealed message, contradicting the purpose of prophethood.
This supports the consensus argument.

برهان الأمانةِ السابقِ ؛ لأنَّ هذا كتمان للحقِّ وخيانة محرَّمةٌ ، وهم أمناء معصومونَ مِنَ المحرَّم أن يُدخِلوهُ في دائرة الوجود بعد معرفتهم نهي مولانا جل وعلا عن ذلكَ
وأما إخفاؤهم شيئاً مِنْ ذلك على طريق النسيان : فالمحققون (۱) أيضاً على منعه ، ودليله : إجماع السلف
وقد صَرَّحَ القرآنُ بكمال التبليغ في حق نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي ﴾ [المائدة : ٣]
وصرَّحَ أيضاً بذلك النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في الحديثِ (۲)
ولم يحضرني الآن لفظ الحديث (٢) .
وصرَّحَ بذلكَ الرُّسُلُ في القرآنِ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ( أُبَلِّغُكُمْ رِسَلَتِ ربي ﴾ [الأعراف : ٤٦٢] ، وقوله جلَّ وعلا: ﴿ لَقَدْ أَبْلَغْتُكُمْ رِسَالَةَ رَبِّي وَنَصَحْتُ لَكُمْ وَلَكِن لَّا تُحِبُّونَ النَّصِحِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ٧٩] ، وقوله تبارك وتعالى : ﴿ لَقَدْ أَبْلَغْتُكُمْ رِسَلَنتِ رَبِّي وَنَصَحْتُ لَكُمْ فَكَيْفَ وَاسَى عَلَى قَوْمٍ كَفِرِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ۹۳] وتتبع نحو ذلك في القرآن كثير(۱) ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق
The proof of the aforementioned trustworthiness: because this is concealment of truth and a forbidden betrayal, and they are trustworthy ones protected from introducing the forbidden into the realm of existence after their knowledge of the prohibition of our Master, Exalted and Glorified, of that. As for their concealing something of that by way of forgetfulness, the investigators (1) also hold its prohibition, and its proof is the consensus of the Salaf. And the Qur'an has explicitly stated the perfection of delivery regarding our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in His saying, Exalted is He: 'This day I have perfected for you your religion and completed upon you My favor' [al-Ma'idah 5:3]. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, also stated that in the hadith (2), and I do not have at hand now the wording of the hadith (2). And the messengers stated that in the Qur'an, such as His saying, Exalted is He: 'I convey to you the messages of my Lord' [al-A'raf 7:62], and His saying, Glorified and Exalted: 'I have conveyed to you the message of my Lord and advised you, but you do not like the advisors' [al-A'raf 7:79], and His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'I have conveyed to you the messages of my Lord and advised you; so how could I grieve over a disbelieving people?' [al-A'raf 7:93]. And similar to that is abundant in the Qur'an (1), and with Allah, Exalted, is success.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage contains a two-part proof for the infallibility of prophets in delivering the message. First, it argues that intentionally hiding the message is forbidden because it is a betrayal; prophets are trustworthy (أمناء) and protected from such. Second, it addresses the possibility of forgetfully omitting the message: the 'investigators' (المحققون) also forbid this, and the evidence is the consensus of the Salaf (إجماع السلف). The author then supports the perfection of delivery with explicit Qur'anic verses: the verse from al-Ma'idah shows the completion of religion for the Prophet Muhammad, and verses from al-A'raf (7:62, 79, 93) show the same for earlier prophets. The passage thus establishes that prophets must deliver the entire message without any omission, whether intentional or forgetful.

إجماع السلف
التبليغ

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that forgetfulness is a natural human trait that could affect prophets without sin.
Correction: The passage argues that even forgetful omission is prohibited by consensus of the Salaf, and thus prophets are protected from it.

Key Takeaway
